the ship that find herself. 
it be her first voyage and though she be but a cargo steamer of twenty five hundred ton she be the very best of her kind the outcome of forty year of experiment and improvement in framework and machinery. and her designer and owner think a much of her a though she have be the lucania. any one can make a float hotel that will pay expense if he put enough money into the saloon and charge for private bath suite of room and such like. but in these day of competition and low freight every square inch of a cargo boat must be build for cheapness great hold capacity and a certain steady speed. this boat be perhaps two hundred and forty foot long and thirty two foot wide with arrangement that enable her to carry cattle on her main and sheep on her upper deck if she want to. but her great glory be the amount of cargo that she could store away in her hold. her owner they be a very well know scotch firm come round with her from the north where she have be launch and christen and fit to liverpool where she be to take cargo for new york. and the owner s daughter miss frazier go to and fro on the clean deck admire the new paint and the brass work and the patent winch and particularly the strong straight bow over which she have crack a bottle of champagne when she name the steamer the dimbula. it be a beautiful september afternoon and the boat in all her newness she be paint lead colour with a red funnel look very fine indeed. her house flag be fly and her whistle from time to time acknowledge the salute of friendly boat who saw that she be new to the high and narrow sea and wish to make her welcome. 
and now say miss frazier delightedly to the captain she s a real ship isn t she. it seem only the other day father give the order for her and now and now isn t she a beauty. the girl be proud of the firm and talk a though she be the control partner. 
oh she s no so bad the skipper reply cautiously. but i m sayin that it take more than christenin to mak a ship. in the nature o thing miss frazier if ye follow me she s just iron and rivet and plate put into the form of a ship. she ha to find herself yet. 
i think father say she be exceptionally well find. 
so she be say the skipper with a laugh. but it s this way wi ship miss frazier. she s all here but the parrts of her have not learn to work together yet. they ve have no chance. 
the engine be work beautifully. i can hear them. 
yes indeed. but there s more than engine to a ship. every inch of her ye ll understand ha to be liven up and make to work wi it neighbour sweetenin her we call it technically. 
and how will you do it. the girl ask. 
we can no more than drive and steer her and so forth. but if we have rough weather this trip it s likely she ll learn the rest by heart. for a ship ye ll obsairve miss frazier be in no sense a reegid body close at both end. she s a highly complex structure o various an conflictin strain wi tissue that must give an tak accordin to her personal modulus of elasteecity. mr. buchanan the chief engineer be come towards them. i m sayin to miss frazier here that our little dimbula ha to be sweeten yet and nothin but a gale will do it. how s all wi your engine buck. 
well enough true by plumb an rule o course. but there s no spontaneeity yet. he turn to the girl. take my word miss frazier and maybe ye ll comprehend late. even after a pretty girl s christen a ship it doe not follow that there s such a thing a a ship under the men that work her. 
i be sayin the very same mr. buchanan the skipper interrupt. 
that s more metaphysical than i can follow say miss frazier laugh. 
why so. ye re good scotch an i know your mother s father he be fra dumfries ye ve a vest right in metapheesics miss frazier just a ye have in the dimbula the engineer say. 
eh well we must go down to the deep watters an earn miss frazier her deevidends. will you not come to my cabin for tea. say the skipper. we ll be in dock the night and when you re goin back to glasgie ye can think of u loadin her down an drivin her forth all for your sake. 
in the next few day they stow some four thousand ton dead weight into the dimbula and take her out from liverpool. a soon a she meet the lift of the open water she naturally begin to talk. if you lay your ear to the side of the cabin the next time you be in a steamer you will hear hundred of little voice in every direction thrill and buzz and whisper and pop and gurgle and sob and squeak exactly like a telephone in a thunder storm. wooden ship shriek and growl and grunt but iron vessel throb and quiver through all their hundred of rib and thousand of rivet. the dimbula be very strongly build and every piece of her have a letter or a number or both to describe it. and every piece have be hammer or forge or roll or punch by man and have live in the roar and rattle of the shipyard for month. therefore every piece have it own separate voice in exact proportion to the amount of trouble spend upon it. cast iron a a rule say very little. but mild steel plate and work iron and rib and beam that have be much bend and weld and rivet talk continuously. their conversation of course be not half a wise a our human talk because they be all though they do not know it bind down one to the other in a black darkness where they cannot tell what be happen near them nor what will overtake them next. 
a soon a she have clear the irish coast a sullen grey head old wave of the atlantic climb leisurely over her straight bow and sit down on the steam capstan use for haul up the anchor. now the capstan and the engine that drive it have be newly paint red and green. besides which nobody like be duck. 
don t you do that again the capstan sputter through the teeth of his cog. hi. where s the fellow go. 
the wave have slouch overside with a plop and a chuckle. but plenty more where he come from say a brother wave and go through and over the capstan who be bolt firmly to an iron plate on the iron deck beam below. 
can t you keep still up there. say the deckbeams. what s the matter with you. one minute you weigh twice a much a you ought to and the next you don t. 
it isn t my fault say the capstan. there s a green brute outside that come and hit me on the head. 
tell that to the shipwright. you ve be in position for month and you ve never wriggle like this before. if you aren t careful you ll strain u. 
talk of strain say a low rasp unpleasant voice be any of you fellow you deck beam we mean aware that those exceedingly ugly knee of yours happen to be rivet into our structure ours. 
who might you be. the deck beam inquire. 
oh nobody in particular be the answer. we re only the port and starboard upper deck stringer. and if you persist in heave and hike like this we shall be reluctantly compel to take step. 
now the stringer of the ship be long iron girder so to speak that run lengthways from stern to bow. they keep the iron frame. what be call rib in a wooden ship. in place and also help to hold the end of the deck beam which go from side to side of the ship. stringer always consider themselves most important because they be so long. 
you will take step will you. this be a long echo rumble. it come from the frame score and score of them each one about eighteen inch distant from the next and each rivet to the stringer in four place. we think you will have a certain amount of trouble in that. and thousand and thousand of the little rivet that hold everything together whisper. you will. you will. stop quiver and be quiet. hold on brother. hold on. hot punch. what s that. 
rivet have no teeth so they cannot chatter with fright. but they do their best a a flutter jar sweep along the ship from stern to bow and she shake like a rat in a terrier s mouth. 
an unusually severe pitch for the sea be rise have lift the big throb screw nearly to the surface and it be spin round in a kind of soda water half sea and half air go much fast than be proper because there be no deep water for it to work in. a it sink again the engine and they be triple expansion three cylinder in a row snort through all their three piston. be that a joke you fellow outside. it s an uncommonly poor one. how be we to do our work if you fly off the handle that way. 
i didn t fly off the handle say the screw twirl huskily at the end of the screw shaft. if i have you d have be scrap iron by this time. the sea drop away from under me and i have nothing to catch on to. that s all. 
that s all d you call it. say the thrust block whose business it be to take the push of the screw. for if a screw have nothing to hold it back it would crawl right into the engine room. it be the hold back of the screw action that give the drive to a ship. i know i do my work deep down and out of sight but i warn you i expect justice. all i ask for be bare justice. why can t you push steadily and evenly instead of whiz like a whirligig and make me hot under all my collar. the thrust block have six collar each face with brass and he do not wish to get them heat. 
all the bearing that support the fifty foot of screw shaft a it run to the stern whisper. justice give u justice. 
i can only give you what i can get the screw answer. look out. it s come again. 
he rise with a roar a the dimbula plunge and whack flack whack whack go the engine furiously for they have little to check them.

the garboard strake be the low plate in the bottom of a ship and the dimbula s garboard strake be nearly three quarter of an inch mild steel.

the tomb of his ancestor. 
some people will tell you that if there be but a single loaf of bread in all india it would be divide equally between the plowdens the trevors the beadons and the rivett carnacs. that be only one way of say that certain family serve india generation after generation a dolphin follow in line across the open sea. 
let u take a small and obscure case. there ha be at least one representative of the devonshire chinns in or near central india since the day of lieutenant fireworker humphrey chinn of the bombay european regiment who assist at the capture of seringapatam in. alfred elli chinn humphrey s young brother command a regiment of bombay grenadier from to when he saw some mix fight. and in john chinn of the same family we will call him john chinn the first come to light a a level head administrator in time of trouble at a place call mundesur. he die young but leave his mark on the new country and the honourable the board of director of the honourable the east india company embody his virtue in a stately resolution and pay for the expense of his tomb among the satpura hill. 
he be succeed by his son lionel chinn who leave the little old devonshire home just in time to be severely wound in the mutiny. he spend his work life within a hundred and fifty mile of john chinn s grave and rise to the command of a regiment of small wild hill men most of whom have know his father. his son john be bear in the small thatch roof mud wall cantonment which be even to day eighty mile from the near railway in the heart of a scrubby tigerish country. colonel lionel chinn serve thirty year and retire. in the canal his steamer pass the outward bind troop ship carry his son eastward to the family duty. 
the chinns be lucky than most folk because they know exactly what they must do. a clever chinn pass for the bombay civil service and get away to central india where everybody be glad to see him. a dull chinn enter the police department or the wood and forest and sooner or late he too appear in central india and that be what give rise to the say central india be inhabit by bhils mairs and chinns all very much alike. the breed be small bone dark and silent and the stupid of them be good shot. john chinn the second be rather clever but a the eldest son he enter the army accord to chinn tradition. his duty be to abide in his father s regiment for the term of his natural life though the corp be one which most men would have pay heavily to avoid. they be irregular small dark and blackish clothe in rifle green with black leather trimming. and friend call them the wuddars which mean a race of low caste people who dig up rat to eat. but the wuddars do not resent it. they be the only wuddars and their point of pride be these. 
firstly they have few english officer than any native regiment. secondly their subaltern be not mount on parade a be the general rule but walk at the head of their men. a man who can hold his own with the wuddars at their quickstep must be sound in wind and limb. thirdly they be the most pukka shikarries. out and out hunter. in all india. fourthly up to one hundredthly they be the wuddars chinn s irregular bhil levy of the old day but now henceforward and for ever the wuddars. 
no englishman enter their mess except for love or through family usage. the officer talk to their soldier in a tongue not two hundred white folk in india understand. and the men be their child all draw from the bhils who be perhaps the strange of the many strange race in india. they be and at heart be wild men furtive shy full of untold superstition. the race whom we call native of the country find the bhil in possession of the land when they first break into that part of the world thousand of year ago. the book call them pre aryan aboriginal dravidian and so forth. and in other word that be what the bhils call themselves. when a rajput chief whose bard can sing his pedigree backwards for twelve hundred year be set on the throne his investiture be not complete till he ha be mark on the forehead with blood from the vein of a bhil. the rajput say the ceremony ha no mean but the bhil know that it be the last last shadow of his old right a the long ago owner of the soil. 
century of oppression and massacre make the bhil a cruel and half crazy thief and cattle stealer and when the english come he seem to be almost a open to civilisation a the tiger of his own jungle. but john chinn the first father of lionel grandfather of our john go into his country live with him learn his language shoot the deer that steal his poor crop and win his confidence so that some bhils learn to plough and sow while others be coax into the company s service to police their friend. 
when they understand that stand in line do not mean instant execution they accept soldier a a cumbrous but amuse kind of sport and be zealous to keep the wild bhils under control. that be the thin edge of the wedge. john chinn the first give them write promise that if they be good from a certain date the government would overlook previous offence. and since john chinn be never know to break his word he promise once to hang a bhil locally esteem invulnerable and hang him in front of his tribe for seven prove murder the bhils settle down a steadily a they know how. it be slow unseen work of the sort that be be do all over india to day. and though john chinn s only reward come a i have say in the shape of a grave at government expense the little people of the hill never forget him. 
colonel lionel chinn know and love them too and they be very fairly civilise for bhils before his service end. many of them could hardly be distinguish from low caste hindoo farmer. but in the south where john chinn the first be bury the wild still cling to the satpura range cherish a legend that some day jan chinn a they call him would return to his own. in the mean time they mistrust the white man and his way. the least excitement would stampede them plunder at random and now and then kill. but if they be handle discreetly they grieve like child and promise never to do it again. 
the bhils of the regiment the uniform men be virtuous in many way but they need humour. they felt bore and homesick unless take after tiger a beater. and their cold blood dare all wuddars shoot tiger on foot. it be their caste mark make even the officer wonder. they would follow up a wound tiger a unconcernedly a though it be a sparrow with a break wing. and this through a country full of cave and rift and pit where a wild beast could hold a dozen men at his mercy. now and then some little man be bring to barrack with his head smash in or his rib tear away. but his companion never learn caution. they content themselves with settle the tiger. 
young john chinn be decant at the verandah of the wuddars lonely mess house from the back seat of a two wheel cart his gun case cascade all round him. the slender little hookey nose boy look forlorn a a stray goat when he slap the white dust off his knee and the cart jolt down the glare road. but in his heart he be content. after all this be the place where he have be bear and thing be not much change since he have be send to england a child fifteen year ago. 
there be a few new building but the air and the smell and the sunshine be the same. and the little green men who cross the parade grind look very familiar. three week ago john chinn would have say he do not remember a word of the bhil tongue but at the mess door he find his lip move in sentence that he do not understand bit of old nursery rhyme and tail end of such order a his father use to give the men. 
the colonel watch him come up the step and laugh.

his son. say the colonel jump up.

his son enter the anteroom in the middle of a fivefold silence. they make him welcome for his father s sake and a they take stock of him for his own. he be ridiculously like the portrait of the colonel on the wall and when he have wash a little of the dust from his throat he go to his quarter with the old man s short noiseless jungle step. 
so much for heredity say the major. that come of four generation among the bhils. 
and the men know it say a wing officer. they ve be wait for this youth with their tongue hang out. i be persuade that unless he absolutely beat em over the head they ll lie down by company and worship him.

young chinn walk like a man in a dream have fetch a compass round the entire cantonment before go to his own tiny cottage. the captain s quarter in which he have be bear delay him for a little. then he look at the well on the parade grind where he have sit of evening with his nurse and at the ten by fourteen church where the officer go to service if a chaplain of any official creed happen to come along. it seem very small a compare with the gigantic building he use to stare up at but it be the same place. 
from time to time he pass a knot of silent soldier who salute. they might have be the very men who have carry him on their back when he be in his first knickerbockers. a faint light burn in his room and a he enter hand clasp his foot and a voice murmur from the floor. 
who be it. say young chinn not know he speak in the bhil tongue. 
i bore you in my arm sahib when i be a strong man and you be a small one cry cry cry. i be your servant a i be your father s before you. we be all your servant. 
young chinn could not trust himself to reply and the voice go on. 
i have take your key from that fat foreigner and send him away. and the stud be in the shirt for mess. who should know if i do not know. and so the baby ha become a man and forget his nurse. but my nephew shall make a good servant or i will beat him twice a day. 
then there rise up with a rattle a straight a a bhil arrow a little white haired wizened ape of a man with medal and order on his tunic stammer salute and tremble. behind him a young and wiry bhil in uniform be take the tree out of chinn s mess boot. 
chinn s eye be full of tear. the old man hold out his key. 
foreigner be bad people. he will never come back again. we be all servant of your father s son. ha the sahib forget who take him to see the trap tiger in the village across the river when his mother be so frighten and he be so brave. 
the scene come back to chinn in great magic lantern flash. bukta. he cry. and all in a breath. you promise nothing should hurt me. be it bukta.

he push forward the hilt of his sword a a sign of service which be an honour pay only to viceroy governor general or to little child whom one love dearly. chinn touch the hilt mechanically with three finger mutter he know not what. it happen to be the old answer of his childhood when bukta in jest call him the little general sahib. 
the major s quarter be opposite chinn s and when he hear his servant gasp with surprise he look across the room. then the major sit on the bed and whistle. for the spectacle of the senior native commission officer of the regiment an unmixed bhil a companion of the order of british india with thirty five year spotless service in the army and a rank among his own people superior to that of many bengal princeling valet the last join subaltern be a little too much for his nerve. 
the throaty bugle blow the mess call that ha a long legend behind it. first a few pierce note like the shriek of beater in a far away cover and next large full and smooth the refrain of the wild song. and oh and oh the green pulse of mundore mundore. 
all little child be in bed when the sahib hear that call last say bukta pass chinn a clean handkerchief. the call bring back memory of his cot under the mosquito net his mother s kiss and the sound of footstep grow faint a he drop asleep among his men. so he hook the dark collar of his new mess jacket and go to dinner like a prince who ha newly inherit his father s crown. 
old bukta swagger forth curl his whisker. he know his own value and no money and no rank within the gift of the government would have induce him to put stud in young officer shirt or to hand them clean tie. yet when he take off his uniform that night and squat among his fellow for a quiet smoke he tell them what he have do and they say that he be entirely right. thereat bukta propound a theory which to a white mind would have seem rave insanity. but the whisper level head little men of war consider it from every point of view and think that there might be a great deal in it. 
at mess under the oil lamp the talk turn a usual to the unfailing subject of shikar big game shoot of every kind and under all sort of condition. young chinn open his eye when he understand that each one of his companion have shoot several tiger in the wuddar style on foot that be make no more of the business than if the brute have be a dog. 
in nine case out of ten say the major a tiger be almost a dangerous a a porcupine. but the tenth time you come home foot first. 
that set all talk and long before midnight chinn s brain be in a whirl with story of tiger man eater and cattle killer each pursue his own business a methodically a clerk in an office. new tiger that have lately come into such and such a district. and old friendly beast of great cunning know by nickname in the mess such a puggy who be lazy with huge paw and mr. malaprop who turn up when you never expect her and make female noise. then they speak of bhil superstition a wide and picturesque field till young chinn hint that they must be pull his leg. 
deed we aren t say a man on his leave. we know all about you. you re a chinn and all that and you ve a sort of vest right here. but if you don t believe what we re tell you what will you do when old bukta begin his story. he know about ghost tiger and tiger that go to a hell of their own. and tiger that walk on their hind foot. and your grandpapa s rid tiger a well. odd he hasn t speak of that yet. 
you know you ve an ancestor bury down satpura way don t you. say the major a chinn smile irresolutely. 
of course i do say chinn who have the chronicle of the book of chinn by heart. it lie in a wear old ledger on the chinese lacquer table behind the piano in the devonshire home and the child be allow to look at it on sunday. 
well i wasn t sure. your revere ancestor my boy accord to the bhils ha a tiger of his own a saddle tiger that he ride round the country whenever he feel incline. i don t call it decent in an ex collector s ghost. but that be what the southern bhils believe. even our men who might be call moderately cool don t care to beat that country if they hear that jan chinn be run about on his tiger. it be suppose to be a cloud animal not stripy but blotchy like a tortoise shell tom cat. no end of a brute it be and a sure sign of war or pestilence or or something. there s a nice family legend for you. 
what s the origin of it d you suppose. say chinn. 
ask the satpura bhils. old jan chinn be a mighty hunter before the lord. perhaps it be the tiger s revenge or perhaps he s huntin em still. you must go to his tomb one of these day and inquire. bukta will probably attend to that. he be ask me before you come whether by any ill luck you have already bag your tiger. if not he be go to enter you under his own wing. of course for you of all men it s imperative. you ll have a first class time with bukta. 
the major be not wrong. bukta keep an anxious eye on young chinn at drill and it be noticeable that the first time the new officer lift up his voice in an order the whole line quiver. even the colonel be take aback for it might have be lionel chinn return from devonshire with a new lease of life. bukta have continue to develop his peculiar theory among his intimate and it be accept a a matter of faith in the line since every word and gesture on young chinn s part so confirm it. 
the old man arrange early that his darling should wipe out the reproach of not have shoot a tiger. but he be not content to take the first or any beast that happen to arrive. in his own village he dispense the high low and middle justice and when his people naked and flutter come to him with word of a beast mark down he bid them send spy to the kill and the water place that he might be sure the quarry be such an one a suit the dignity of such a man. 
three or four time the reckless tracker return most truthfully say that the beast be mangy undersized a tigress wear with nurse or a break toothed old male and bukta would curb young chinn s impatience. 
at last a noble animal be mark down a ten foot cattle killer with a huge roll of loose skin along the belly glossy hide full frilled about the neck whisker frisky and young. he have slay a man in pure sport they say. 
let him be feed quoth bukta and the villager dutifully drive out a cow to amuse him that he might lie up near by. 
prince and potentate have take ship to india and spend great money for the mere glimpse of beast one half a fine a this of bukta s. 
it be not good say he to the colonel when he ask for shoot leave that my colonel s son who may be that my colonel s son should lose his maidenhead on any small jungle beast. that may come after. i have wait long for this which be a tiger. he ha come in from the mair country. in seven day we will return with the skin. 
the mess gnash their teeth enviously. bukta have he choose might have invite them all. but he go out alone with chinn two day in a shoot cart and a day on foot till they come to a rocky glary valley with a pool of good water in it. it be a parch day and the boy very naturally strip and go in for a bathe leave bukta by the clothe. a white skin show far against brown jungle and what bukta behold on chinn s back and right shoulder drag him forward step by step with star eyeball. 
i d forget it isn t decent to strip before a man of his position say chinn flounce in the water. how the little devil stare. what be it bukta. the mark. be the whisper answer. 
it be nothing. you know how it be with my people. chinn be annoy. the dull red birth mark on his shoulder something like a conventionalise tartar cloud have slip his memory or he would not have bath. it occur so they say at home in alternate generation appear curiously enough eight or nine year after birth and save that it be part of the chinn inheritance would not be consider pretty. he hurry ashore dress again and go on till they meet two or three bhils who promptly fell on their face. my people grunt bukta not condescend to notice them. and so your people sahib. when i be a young man we be few but not so weak. now we be many but poor stock. a may be remember. how will you shoot him sahib. from a tree. from a shelter which my people shall build. by day or by night. 
on foot and in the daytime say young chinn. 
that be your custom a i have hear say bukta to himself i will get news of him. then you and i will go to him. i will carry one gun. you have yours. there be no need of more. what tiger shall stand against thee. 
he be mark down by a little water hole at the head of a ravine full gorge and half asleep in the may sunlight. he be walk up like a partridge and he turn to do battle for his life. bukta make no motion to raise his rifle but keep his eye on chinn who meet the shatter roar of the charge with a single shoot it seem to him hour a he sight which tear through the throat smash the backbone below the neck and between the shoulder. the brute couch choke and fell and before chinn know well what have happen bukta bid him stay still while he pace the distance between his foot and the ring jaw. 
fifteen say bukta. short pace. no need for a second shoot sahib. he bleed cleanly where he lie and we need not spoil the skin. i say there would be no need of these but they come in case. 
suddenly the side of the ravine be crown with the head of bukta s people a force that could have blow the rib out of the beast have chinn s shoot fail. but their gun be hide and they appear a interest beater some five or six wait the word to skin. bukta watch the life fade from the wild eye lift one hand and turn on his heel. 
no need to show that we care say he. now after this we can kill what we choose. put out your hand sahib. 
chinn obey. it be entirely steady and bukta nod. that also be your custom. my men skin quickly. they will carry the skin to cantonment. will the sahib come to my poor village for the night and perhaps forget that i be his officer. 
but those men the beater. they have work hard and perhaps. 
oh if they skin clumsily we will skin them. they be my people. in the line i be one thing. here i be another. 
this be very true. when bukta doff uniform and revert to the fragmentary dress of his own people he leave his civilisation of drill in the next world. that night after a little talk with his subject he devote to an orgie. and a bhil orgie be a thing not to be safely write about. chinn flush with triumph be in the thick of it but the mean of the mystery be hide. wild folk come and press about his knee with offering. he give his flask to the elder of the village. they grow eloquent and wreathe him about with flower. gift and loan not all seemly be thrust upon him and infernal music roll and madden round red fire while singer sing song of the ancient time and dance peculiar dance. the aboriginal liquor be very potent and chinn be compel to taste them often but unless the stuff have be drug how come he to fall asleep suddenly and to waken late the next day half a march from the village. 
the sahib be very tire. a little before dawn he go to sleep bukta explain. my people carry him here and now it be time we should go back to cantonment. 
the voice smooth and deferential the step steady and silent make it hard to believe that only a few hour before bukta be yell and caper with naked fellow devil of the scrub. 
my people be very please to see the sahib. they will never forget. when next the sahib go out recruit he will go to my people and they will give him a many men a we need. 
chinn keep his own counsel except a to the shoot of the tiger and bukta embroider that tale with a shameless tongue. the skin be certainly one of the fine ever hang up in the mess and the first of many. when bukta could not accompany his boy on shoot trip he take care to put him in good hand and chinn learn more of the mind and desire of the wild bhil in his march and camping by talk at twilight or at wayside pool than an uninstructed man could have come at in a lifetime. 
presently his men in the regiment grow bold to speak of their relative mostly in trouble and to lay case of tribal custom before him. they would say squat in his verandah at twilight after the easy confidential style of the wuddars that such and such a bachelor have run away with such and such a wife at a far off village. now how many cow would chinn sahib consider a just fine. or again if write order come from the government that a bhil be to repair to a wall city of the plain to give evidence in a law court would it be wise to disregard that order. on the other hand if it be obey would the rash voyager return alive. 
but what have i to do with these thing. chinn demand of bukta impatiently. i be a soldier. i do not know the law. 
hoo. law be for fool and white men. give them a large and loud order and they will abide by it. thou art their law. 
but wherefore. 
every trace of expression leave bukta s countenance. the idea might have smite him for the first time. how can i say. he reply. perhaps it be on account of the name. a bhil doe not love strange thing. give them order sahib two three four word at a time such a they can carry away in their head. that be enough. 
chinn give order then valiantly not realise that a word speak in haste before mess become the dread unappealable law of village beyond the smoky hill be in truth no le than the law of jan chinn the first who so the whisper legend run have come back to earth to oversee the third generation in the body and bone of his grandson. 
there could be no sort of doubt in this matter. all the bhils know that jan chinn reincarnate have honour bukta s village with his presence after slay his first in this life tiger. that he have eat and drink with the people a he be use. and bukta must have drug chinn s liquor very deeply upon his back and right shoulder all men have see the same angry red fly cloud that the high god have set on the flesh of jan chinn the first when first he come to the bhil. a concern the foolish white world which ha no eye he be a slim and young officer in the wuddars. but his own people know he be jan chinn who have make the bhil a man. and believe they hasten to carry his word careful never to alter them on the way. 
because the savage and the child who play lonely game have one horror of be laugh at or question the little folk keep their conviction to themselves. and the colonel who think he know his regiment never guess that each one of the six hundred quick foot beady eye rank and file to attention beside their rifle believe serenely and unshakenly that the subaltern on the leave flank of the line be a demi god twice bear tutelary deity of their land and people. the earth god themselves have stamp the incarnation and who would dare to doubt the handiwork of the earth god. 
chinn be practical above all thing saw that his family name serve him well in the line and in camp. his men give no trouble one doe not commit regimental offence with a god in the chair of justice and he be sure of the best beater in the district when he need them. they believe that the protection of jan chinn the first cloak them and be bold in that belief beyond the utmost dare of excite bhils. 
his quarter begin to look like an amateur natural history museum in spite of duplicate head and horn and skull that he send home to devonshire. the people very humanly learn the weak side of their god. it be true he be unbribable but bird skin butterfly beetle and above all news of big game please him. in other respect too he live up to the chinn tradition. he be fever proof. a night s sit out over a tether goat in a damp valley that would have fill the major with a month s malaria have no effect on him. he be a they say salt before he be bear. 
now in the autumn of his second year s service an uneasy rumour creep out of the earth and run about among the bhils. chinn hear nothing of it till a brother officer say across the mess table. your revere ancestor s on the rampage in the satpura country. you d good look him up. 
i don t want to be disrespectful but i m a little sick of my revere ancestor. bukta talk of nothing else. what s the old boy suppose to be do now. 
rid cross country by moonlight on his processional tiger. that s the story. he s be see by about two thousand bhils skip along the top of the satpuras and scar people to death. they believe it devoutly and all the satpura chap be worship away at his shrine tomb i mean like good un. you really ought to go down there. must be a queer thing to see your grandfather treat a a god.

a command officer be generally aware of the regimental state of mind a little before the men. and this be why the colonel say a few day late that some one have be put the fear of god into the wuddars. a he be the only person officially entitle to do this it distress him to see such unanimous virtue. it s too good to last he say. i only wish i could find out what the little chap mean.

it be a good kowl say the leader. first the chaplain who laugh take away our plunder and beat three of u a be promise. next we meet fawne sahib who frown and ask for the plunder. we speak the truth and so he beat u all one after another and call u choose name. he then give u these two bundle they set down a bottle of whisky and a box of cheroot and we come away. the kowl be leave in a tree because it virtue be that so soon a we show it to a sahib we be beat.

it be write in the chronicle of the satpura bhils together with many other matter not fit for print that through five day after the day that he have put his mark upon them jan chinn the first hunt for his people. and on the five night of those day the tribe be gloriously and entirely drink. jan chinn buy country spirit of an awful strength and slew wild pig and deer beyond count so that if any fell sick they might have two good reason. 
between head and stomach ache they find no time to think of their arm but follow jan chinn obediently through the jungle and with each day s return confidence men woman and child steal away to their village a the little army pass by. they carry news that it be good and right to be scratch with ghost knife. that jan chinn be indeed reincarnate a a god of free food and drink and that of all nation the satpura bhils stand first in his favour if they would only refrain from scratch. henceforward that kindly demi god would be connect in their mind with great gorge and the vaccine and lancet of a paternal government.

come out then chinn shout. come out of that. let s have a look at you. the brute know well enough that there be some connection between brown nude bhils and his weekly allowance. but the white helmet in the sunlight annoy him and he do not approve of the voice that break his rest. lazily a a gorge snake he drag himself out of the cave and stand yawn and blink at the entrance. the sunlight fell upon his flat right side and chinn wonder. never have he see a tiger mark after this fashion. except for his head which be staringly bar he be dapple not strip but dapple like a child s rock horse in rich shade of smoky black on red gold. that portion of his belly and throat which should have be white be orange and his tail and paw be black. 
he look leisurely for some ten second and then deliberately lower his head his chin drop and draw in star intently at the man. the effect of this be to throw forward the round arch of his skull with two broad band across it while below the band glare the unwinking eye. so that head on a he stand he show something like a diabolically scowl pantomime mask. it be a piece of natural mesmerism that he have practise many time on his quarry and though chinn be by no mean a terrify heifer he stand for a while hold by the extraordinary oddity of the attack. the head the body seem to have be pack away behind it the ferocious skull like head creep near to the switch of an angry tail tip in the grass. leave and right the bhils have scatter to let john chinn subdue his own horse. 
my word. he think. he s try to frighten me. and fire between the saucer like eye leap aside upon the shoot. 
a big cough mass reek of carrion bound past him up the hill and he follow discreetly. the tiger make no attempt to turn into the jungle. he be hunt for sight and breath nose up mouth open the tremendous fore leg scatter the gravel in spurt. 
scupper. say john chinn watch the flight. now if he be a partridge he d tower. lung must be full of blood. 
the brute have jerk himself over a boulder and fall out of sight the other side. john chinn look over with a ready barrel. but the red trail lead straight a an arrow even to his grandfather s tomb and there among the smash spirit bottle and the fragment of the mud image the life leave with a flurry and a grunt. 
if my worthy ancestor could see that say john chinn he d have be proud of me. eye low jaw and lung. a very nice shoot. he whistle for bukta a he draw the tape over the stiffen bulk. 
ten six eight by jove. it s nearly eleven call it eleven. fore arm twenty four five seven and a half. a short tail too. three foot one. but what a skin. oh bukta. bukta. the men with the knife swiftly. 
be he beyond question dead. say an awe stricken voice behind a rock. 
that be not the way i kill my first tiger say chinn. i do not think that bukta would run. i have no second gun. 
it it be the cloud tiger say bukta un heed the taunt. 
he be dead. 
whether all the bhils vaccinate and unvaccinated of the satpuras have lie by to see the kill chinn could not say. but the whole hill s flank rustle with little men shout sing and stamp. and yet till he have make the first cut in the splendid skin not a man would take a knife. and when the shadow fell they run from the red stain tomb and no persuasion would bring them back till dawn. so chinn spend a second night in the open guard the carcass from jackal and think about his ancestor. 
he return to the lowland to the triumphal chant of an escort army three hundred strong the mahratta vaccinator close at his elbow and the rudely dry skin a trophy before him. when that army suddenly and noiselessly disappear a quail in high corn he argue he be near civilisation and a turn in the road bring him upon the camp of a wing of his own corp. he leave the skin on a cart tail for the world to see and seek the colonel. 
they re perfectly right he explain earnestly. there isn t an ounce of vice in em. they be only frighten. i ve vaccinate the whole boil and they like it awfully. what be what be we do here sir. 
that s what i m try to find out say the colonel. i don t know yet whether we re a piece of a brigade or a police force. however i think we ll call ourselves a police force. how do you manage to get a bhil vaccinate. 
well sir say chinn i ve be think it over and a far a i can make out i ve get a sort of hereditary influence over em. 
so i know or i wouldn t have send you. but what exactly. 
it s rather rummy. it seem from what i can make out that i m my own grandfather reincarnate and i ve be disturb the peace of the country by rid a pad tiger of night. if i hadn t do that i don t think they d have object to the vaccination. but the two together be more than they could stand. and so sir i ve vaccinate em and shoot my tiger horse a a sort o proof of good faith. you never saw such a skin in your life. 
the colonel tug his moustache think fully. now how the deuce say he be i to include that in my report. 
indeed the official version of the bhils anti vaccination stampede say nothing about lieutenant john chinn his godship. but bukta know and the corp know and every bhil in the satpura hill know. 
and now bukta be zealous that john chinn shall swiftly be wed and impart his power to a son. for if the chinn succession fail and the little bhils be leave to their own imagine there will be fresh trouble in the satpuras. 
the devil and the deep sea. 
all supply very bad and dear and there be no facility for even the small repair. sail direction. 
her nationality be british but you will not find her house flag in the list of our mercantile marine. she be a nine hundred ton iron schooner rig screw cargo boat differ externally in no way from any other tramp of the sea. but it be with steamer a it be with men. there be those who will for a consideration sail extremely close to the wind. and in the present state of a fall world such people and such steamer have their use. from the hour that the aglaia first enter the clyde new shiny and innocent with a quart of cheap champagne trickle down her cut water fate and her owner who be also her captain decree that she should deal with embarrass crown head flee president financier of over extend ability woman to whom change of air be imperative and the less law break power. her career lead her sometimes into the admiralty court where the swear statement of her skipper fill his brother with envy. the mariner cannot tell or act a lie in the face of the sea or mi lead a tempest. but a lawyer have discover he make up for chance withhold when he return to shore an affidavit in either hand. 
the aglaia figure with distinction in the great mackinaw salvage case. it be her first slip from virtue and she learn how to change her name but not her heart and to run across the sea. a the guide light she be very badly want in a south american port for the little matter of enter harbour at full speed collide with a coal hulk and the state s only man of war just a that man of war be go to coal. she put to sea without explanation though three fort fire at her for half an hour. a the julia m gregor she have be concern in pick up from a raft certain gentleman who should have stay in noumea but who prefer make themselves vastly unpleasant to authority in quite another quarter of the world. and a the shah in shah she have be overtake on the high sea indecently full of munition of war by the cruiser of an agitate power at issue with it neighbour. that time she be very nearly sink and her riddle hull give eminent lawyer of two country great profit. after a season she reappear a the martin hunt paint a dull slate colour with pure saffron funnel and boat of robin s egg blue engage in the odessa trade till she be invite. and the invitation could not well be disregard. to keep away from black sea port altogether. 
she have ride through many wave of depression. freight might drop out of sight seaman s union throw spanner and nut at certificate master or stevedore combine till cargo perish on the dock head. but the boat of many name come and go busy alert and inconspicuous always. her skipper make no complaint of hard time and port officer observe that her crew sign and sign again with the regularity of atlantic liner boatswain. her name she change a occasion call. her well pay crew never. and a large percentage of the profit of her voyage be spend with an open hand on her engine room. she never trouble the underwriter and very seldom stop to talk with a signal station for her business be urgent and private. 
but an end come to her trading and she perish in this manner. deep peace brood over europe asia africa america australasia and polynesia. the power deal together more or le honestly. bank pay their depositor to the hour. diamond of price come safely to the hand of their owner. republic rest content with their dictator. diplomat find no one whose presence in the least incommode them. monarch live openly with their lawfully wed wife. it be a though the whole earth have put on it best sunday bib and tucker. and business be very bad for the martin hunt. the great virtuous calm engulf her slate side yellow funnel and all but cast up in another hemisphere the steam whaler haliotis black and rusty with a manure colour funnel a litter of dingy white boat and an enormous stave or furnace for boil blubber on her forward well deck. there could be no doubt that her trip be successful for she lay at several port not too well know and the smoke of her try out insult the beach. 
anon she depart at the speed of the average london four wheeler and enter a semi inland sea warm still and blue which be perhaps the most strictly preserve water in the world. there she stay for a certain time and the great star of those mild sky behold her play pus in the corner among island where whale be never find. all that while she smelt abominably and the smell though fishy be not whalesome. one even calamity descend upon her from the island of pygang watai and she flee while her crew jeer at a fat black and brown gunboat puff far behind. they know to the last revolution the capacity of every boat on those sea that they be anxious to avoid. a british ship with a good conscience doe not a a rule flee from the man of war of a foreign power and it be also consider a breach of etiquette to stop and search british ship at sea. these thing the skipper of the haliotis do not pause to prove but hold on at an inspirit eleven knot an hour till nightfall. one thing only he overlook. 
the power that keep an expensive steam patrol move up and down those water. they have dodge the two regular ship of the station with an ease that breed contempt. have newly bring up a third and a fourteen knot boat with a clean bottom to help the work. and that be why the haliotis drive hard from the east to the west find herself at daylight in such a position that she could not help see an arrangement of four flag a mile and a half behind which read. heave to or take the consequence. 
she have her choice and she take it. the end come when presume on her light draught she try to draw away northward over a friendly shoal. the shell that arrive by way of the chief engineer s cabin be some five inch in diameter with a practice not a burst charge. it have be intend to cross her bow and that be why it knock the frame portrait of the chief engineer s wife and she be a very pretty girl on to the floor splinter his wash hand stand cross the alleyway into the engine room and strike on a grate drop directly in front of the forward engine where it burst neatly fracture both the bolt that hold the connect rod to the forward crank. 
what follow be worth consideration. the forward engine have no more work to do. it release piston rod therefore drive up fiercely with nothing to check it and start most of the nut of the cylinder cover. it come down again the full weight of the steam behind it and the foot of the disconnect connect rod useless a the leg of a man with a sprain ankle fling out to the right and strike the starboard or right hand cast iron support column of the forward engine crack it clean through about six inch above the base and wedge the upper portion outwards three inch towards the ship s side. there the connect rod jam. meantime the after engine be a yet unembarrassed go on with it work and in so do bring round at it next revolution the crank of the forward engine which smite the already jam connect rod bend it and therewith the piston rod cross head the big cross piece that slide up and down so smoothly. 
the cross head jam sideways in the guide and in addition to put further pressure on the already break starboard support column crack the port or leave hand support column in two or three place. there be nothing more that could be make to move the engine bring up all stand with a hiccup that seem to lift the haliotis a foot out of the water. and the engine room staff open every steam outlet that they could find in the confusion arrive on deck somewhat scald but calm. there be a sound below of thing happen a rush click purr grunt rattle noise that do not last for more than a minute. it be the machinery adjust itself on the spur of the moment to a hundred alter condition. mr. wardrop one foot on the upper grate incline his ear sideways and groan. you cannot stop engine work at twelve knot an hour in three second without disorganise them. the haliotis slide forward in a cloud of steam shriek like a wound horse. there be nothing more to do. the five inch shell with a reduce charge have settle the situation. and when you be full all three hold of strictly preserve pearl. when you have clean out the tanna bank the sea horse bank and four other bank from one end to the other of the amanala sea when you have rip out the very heart of a rich government monopoly so that five year will not repair your wrong do you must smile and take what be in store. but the skipper reflect a a launch put out from the man of war that he have be bombard on the high sea with the british flag several of them picturesquely dispose above him and try to find comfort from the think. 
where say the stolid naval lieutenant hoist himself aboard where be those dam pearl. 
they be there beyond evasion. no affidavit could do away with the fearful smell of decay oyster the dive dress and the shell litter hatch. they be there to the value of seventy thousand pound more or le. and every pound poach. 
the man of war be annoy. for she have use up many ton of coal she have strain her tube and bad than all her officer and crew have be hurry. every one on the haliotis be arrest and rearrested several time a each officer come aboard. then they be tell by what they esteem to be the equivalent of a midshipman that they be to consider themselves prisoner and finally be put under arrest.

god know. and this prize lieutenant s drink. what do you think you can do.

the skipper never interfere with the affair of the engine room and mr. wardrop an artist in his profession turn to and compose a work terrible and forbid. his background be the dark grain side of the engine room. his material the metal of power and strength help out with spar baulk and rope. the man of war tow sullenly and viciously. the haliotis behind her hum like a hive before swarm. with extra and totally unneeded spar her crew block up the space round the forward engine till it resemble a statue in it scaffold and the butt of the shore interfere with every view that a dispassionate eye might wish to take. and that the dispassionate mind might be swiftly shake out of it calm the well sink bolt of the shore be wrap round untidily with loose end of rope give a study effect of most dangerous insecurity. next mr. wardrop take up a collection from the after engine which a you will remember have not be affect in the general wreck. the cylinder escape valve he abolish with a flog hammer. it be difficult in far off port to come by such valve unless like mr. wardrop you keep duplicate in store. at the same time men take off the nut of two of the great hold down bolt that serve to keep the engine in place on their solid bed. an engine violently arrest in mid career may easily jerk off the nut of a hold down bolt and this accident look very natural. 
pass along the tunnel he remove several shaft couple bolt and nut scatter other and ancient piece of iron underfoot. cylinder bolt he cut off to the number of six from the after engine cylinder so that it might match it neighbour and stuff the bilge and fee pump with cotton waste. then he make up a neat bundle of the various odds and end that he have gather from the engine little thing like nut and valve spindle all carefully tallowed and retire with them under the floor of the engine room where he sigh be fat a he pass from manhole to manhole of the double bottom and in a fairly dry submarine compartment hide them. any engineer particularly in an unfriendly port ha a right to keep his spare store where he choose. and the foot of one of the cylinder shore block all entrance into the regular store room even if that have not be already close with steel wedge. in conclusion he disconnect the after engine lay piston and connect rod carefully tallowed where it would be most inconvenient to the casual visitor take out three of the eight collar of the thrust block hide them where only he could find them again fill the boiler by hand wedge the slide door of the coal bunker and rest from his labour. the engine room be a cemetery and it do not need the content of the ash lift through the skylight to make it any bad. 
he invite the skipper to look at the complete work.

it be the fire that do it. they should have keep their counsel. but when a few thousand foreigner be burst with joy over the fact that a ship under the british flag ha be fire at on the high sea news travel quickly. and when it come out that the pearl steal crew have not be allow access to their consul. there be no consul within a few hundred mile of that lonely port. even the friendly of power ha a right to ask question. the great heart of the british public be beat furiously on account of the performance of a notorious race horse and have not a throb to waste on distant accident. but somewhere deep in the hull of the ship of state there be machinery which more or le accurately take charge of foreign affair. that machinery begin to revolve and who so shock and surprise a the power that have capture the haliotis. it explain that colonial governor and far away men of war be difficult to control and promise that it would most certainly make an example both of the governor and the vessel. a for the crew report to be press into military service in tropical clime it would produce them a soon a possible and it would apologise if necessary. now no apology be need. when one nation apologise to another million of amateur who have no earthly concern with the difficulty hurl themselves into the strife and embarrass the train specialist. it be request that the crew be find if they be still alive they have be eight month beyond knowledge and it be promise that all would be forget. 
the little governor of the little port be please with himself. seven and twenty white men make a very compact force to throw away on a war that have neither begin nor end a jungle and stockade fight that flicker and smoulder through the wet hot year in the hill a hundred mile away and be the heritage of every weary official. he have he think deserve well of his country. and if only some one would buy the unhappy haliotis moor in the harbour below his verandah his cup would be full. he look at the neatly silver lamp that he have take from her cabin and think of much that might be turn to account. but his countryman in that moist climate have no spirit. they would peep into the silent engine room and shake their head. even the men of war would not tow her further up the coast where the governor believe that she could be repair. she be a bad bargain. but her cabin carpet be undeniably beautiful and his wife approve of her mirror. 
three hour late cable be burst round him like shell for though he know it not he be be offer a a sacrifice by the nether to the upper millstone and his superior have no regard for his feeling. he have say the cable grossly exceed his power and fail to report on event. he would therefore at this he cast himself back in his hammock produce the crew of the haliotis. he would send for them and if that fail he would put his dignity on a pony and fetch them himself. he have no conceivable right to make pearl poacher serve in any war. he would be hold responsible. 
next morning the cable wish to know whether he have find the crew of the haliotis. they be to be find free and feed he be to fee them till such time a they could be send to the near english port in a man of war. if you abuse a man long enough in great word flash over the sea bed thing happen. the governor send inland swiftly for his prisoner who be also soldier. and never be a militia regiment more anxious to reduce it strength. no power short of death could make these mad men wear the uniform of their service. they would not fight except with their fellow and it be for that reason the regiment have not go to war but stay in a stockade reason with the new troop. the autumn campaign have be a fiasco but here be the englishman. all the regiment march back to guard them and the hairy enemy arm with blow pipe rejoice in the forest. five of the crew have die but there line up on the governor s verandah two and twenty men mark about the leg with the scar of leech bite. a few of them wear fringe that have once be trouser. the others use loin cloth of gay pattern. and they exist beautifully but simply in the governor s verandah and when he come out they sing at him. when you have lose seventy thousand pound worth of pearl your pay your ship and all your clothe and have live in bondage for five month beyond the faint pretence of civilisation you know what true independence mean for you become the happy of create thing natural man. 
the governor tell the crew that they be evil and they ask for food. when he saw how they eat and when he remember that none of the pearl patrol boat be expect for two month he sigh. but the crew of the haliotis lay down in the verandah and say that they be pensioner of the governor s bounty. a grey beard man fat and bald head his one garment a green and yellow loin cloth saw the haliotis in the harbour and bellow for joy. the men crowd to the verandah rail kick aside the long cane chair. they point gesticulate and argue freely without shame. the militia regiment sit down in the governor s garden. the governor retire to his hammock it be a easy to be kill lie a stand and his woman squeak from the shutter room.

in his simple way the governor be a strategist. he do not desire that the crew of the haliotis should come ashore again either singly or in detachment and he propose to turn their steamer into a convict hulk. they would wait he explain this from the quay to the skipper in the barge and they would continue to wait till the man of war come along exactly where they be. if one of them set foot ashore the entire regiment would open fire and he would not scruple to use the two cannon of the town. meantime food would be send daily in a boat under an arm escort. the skipper bare to the waist and row could only grind his teeth. and the governor improve the occasion and revenge himself for the bitter word in the cable by say what he think of the moral and manner of the crew. the barge return to the haliotis in silence and the skipper climb aboard white on the cheek bone and blue about the nostril.

then the skipper curse mr. wardrop for import frivolous side issue into the conversation. and the crew curse one another and the haliotis the voyage and all that they know or could bring to mind. they sit down in silence on the empty deck and their eye burn in their head. the green harbour water chuckle at them overside. they look at the palm fringe hill inland at the white house above the harbour road at the single tier of native craft by the quay at the stolid soldiery sit round the two cannon and last of all at the blue bar of the horizon. mr. wardrop be bury in think and scratch imaginary line with his untrimmed finger nail on the plank.
