captain i ll trouble you for the rest of the men a i want them. we ll get my store out and clear away the shore we don t need and then we ll patch her up. my men will remember that they re in the haliotis under me. 
he go into the engine room and the others star. they be use to the accident of the sea but this be beyond their experience. none who have see the engine room believe that anything short of new engine from end to end could stir the haliotis from her mooring. 
the engine room store be unearth and mr. wardrop s face red with the filth of the bilge and the exertion of travel on his stomach light with joy. the spare gear of the haliotis have be unusually complete and two and twenty men arm with screw jack differential block tackle vice and a forge or so can look kismet between the eye without wink. the crew be order to replace the hold down and shaft bear bolt and return the collar of the thrust block. when they have finish mr. wardrop deliver a lecture on repair compound engine without the aid of the shop and the men sit about on the cold machinery. the cross head jam in the guide leer at them drunkenly but offer no help. they run their finger hopelessly into the crack of the starboard support column and pick at the end of the rope round the shore while mr. wardrop s voice rise and fell echo till the quick tropic night close down over the engine room skylight. 
next morning the work of reconstruction begin. it ha be explain that the foot of the connect rod be force against the foot of the starboard support column which it have crack through and drive outward towards the ship s skin. to all appearance the job be more than hopeless for rod and column seem to have be weld into one. but herein providence smile on them for one moment to hearten them through the weary week ahead. the second engineer more reckless than resourceful strike at random with a cold chisel into the cast iron of the column and a greasy grey flake of metal fly from under the imprison foot of the connect rod while the rod itself fell away slowly and bring up with a thunderous clang somewhere in the dark of the crank pit. the guide plate above be still jam fast in the guide but the first blow have be strike. they spend the rest of the day groom the donkey engine which stand immediately forward of the engine room hatch. it tarpaulin of course have be steal and eight warm month have not improve the work part. further the last die hiccup of the haliotis seem or it might have be the malay from the boat house to have lift the thing bodily on it bolt and set it down inaccurately a regard it steam connection. 
if we only have one single cargo derrick. mr. wardrop sigh. we can take the cylinder cover off by hand if we sweat. but to get the rod out o the piston s not possible unless we use steam. well there ll be steam the morn if there s nothing else. she ll fizzle. 
next morning men from the shore saw the haliotis through a cloud for it be a though the deck smoke. her crew be chase steam through the shake and leaky pipe to it work in the forward donkey engine. and where oakum fail to plug a crack they strip off their loin cloth for lap and swear half boil and mother naked. the donkey engine work at a price the price of constant attention and furious stoke work long enough to allow a wire rope. it be make up of a funnel and a foremast stay. to be lead into the engine room and make fast on the cylinder cover of the forward engine. that rise easily enough and be haul through the skylight and on to the deck many hand assist the doubtful steam. then come the tug of war for it be necessary to get to the piston and the jam piston rod. they remove two of the piston junk ring stud screw in two strong iron eye bolt by way of handle double the wire rope and set half a dozen men to smite with an extemporise batter ram at the end of the piston rod where it peer through the piston while the donkey engine haul upwards on the piston itself. after four hour of this furious work the piston rod suddenly slip and the piston rise with a jerk knock one or two men over into the engine room. but when mr. wardrop declare that the piston have not split they cheer and think nothing of their wound. and the donkey engine be hastily stop. it boiler be nothing to tamper with. 
and day by day their supply reach them by boat. the skipper humble himself once more before the governor and a a concession have leave to get drink water from the malay boat builder on the quay. it be not good drink water but the malay be anxious to supply anything in his power if he be pay for it. 
now when the jaw of the forward engine stand a it be strip and empty they begin to wedge up the shore of the cylinder itself. that work alone fill the good part of three day warm and sticky day when the hand slip and sweat run into the eye. when the last wedge be hammer home there be no long an ounce of weight on the support column. and mr. wardrop rummage the ship for boiler plate three quarter of an inch thick where he could find it. there be not much available but what there be be more than beat gold to him. in one desperate forenoon the entire crew naked and lean hale back more or le into place the starboard support column which a you remember be crack clean through. mr. wardrop find them asleep where they have finish the work and give them a day s rest smile upon them a a father while he draw chalk mark about the crack. they wake to new and more try labour. for over each one of those crack a plate of three quarter inch boiler iron be to be work hot the rivet hole be drill by hand. all that time they be feed on fruit chiefly banana with some sago. 
those be the day when men swoon over the ratchet drill and the hand forge and where they fell they have leave to lie unless their body be in the way of their fellow foot. and so patch upon patch and a patch over all the starboard support column be clout. but when they think all be secure mr. wardrop decree that the noble patchwork would never support work engine. at the best it could only hold the guide bar approximately true he deadweight of the cylinder must be bear by vertical strut. and therefore a gang would repair to the bow and take out with file the big bow anchor davit each of which be some three inch in diameter. they throw hot coal at wardrop and threaten to kill him those who do not weep. they be ready to weep on the least provocation. but he hit them with iron bar heat at the end and they limp forward and the davit come with them when they return. they sleep sixteen hour on the strength of it and in three day two strut be in place bolt from the foot of the starboard support column to the under side of the cylinder. there remain now the port or condenser column which though not so badly crack a it fellow have also be strengthen in four place with boiler plate patch but need strut. they take away the main stanchion of the bridge for that work and crazy with toil do not see till all be in place that the round bar of iron must be flatten from top to bottom to allow the air pump lever to clear them. it be wardrop s oversight and he weep bitterly before the men a he give the order to unbolt the strut and flatten them with hammer and the flame. now the break engine be underpin firmly and they take away the wooden shore from under the cylinder and give them to the rob bridge thank god for even half a day s work on gentle kindly wood instead of the iron that have enter into their soul. eight month in the back country among the leech at a temperature of degree moist be very bad for the nerve. 
they have keep the hard work to the last a boy save latin prose and wear though they be mr. wardrop do not dare to give them rest. the piston rod and connect rod be to be straighten and this be a job for a regular dockyard with every appliance. they fell to it cheer by a little chalk show of work do and time consume which mr. wardrop write up on the engine room bulkhead. fifteen day have go fifteen day of kill labour and there be hope before them. 
it be curious that no man know how the rod be straighten. the crew of the haliotis remember that week very dimly a a fever patient remember the delirium of a long night. there be fire everywhere they say. the whole ship be one consume furnace and the hammer be never still. now there could not have be more than one fire at the most for mr. wardrop distinctly recall that no straighten be do except under his own eye. they remember too that for many year voice give order which they obey with their body but their mind be abroad on all the sea. it seem to them that they stand through day and night slowly slide a bar backwards and forward through a white glow that be part of the ship. they remember an intolerable noise in their burn head from the wall of the stoke hole and they remember be savagely beat by men whose eye seem asleep. when their shift be over they would draw straight line in the air anxiously and repeatedly and would question one another in their sleep cry be she straight. 
at last they do not remember whether this be by day or by night mr. wardrop begin to dance clumsily and weep the while. and they too dance and weep and go to sleep twitch all over. and when they wake men say that the rod be straighten and no one do any work for two day but lay on the deck and eat fruit. mr. wardrop would go below from time to time and pat the two rod where they lay and they hear him sing hymn. 
then his trouble of mind go from him and at the end of the third day s idleness he make a draw in chalk upon the deck with letter of the alphabet at the angle. he point out that though the piston rod be more or le straight the piston rod cross head the thing that have be jam sideways in the guide have be badly strain and have crack the low end of the piston rod. he be go to forge and shrink a work iron collar on the neck of the piston rod where it join the cross head and from the collar he would bolt a y shape piece of iron whose low arm should be bolt into the cross head. if anything more be need they could use up the last of the boiler plate. 
so the forge be light again and men burn their body but hardly felt the pain. the finish connection be not beautiful but it seem strong enough at least a strong a the rest of the machinery. and with that job their labour come to an end. all that remain be to connect up the engine and to get food and water. the skipper and four men deal with the malay boat builder by night chiefly. it be no time to haggle over the price of sago and dry fish. the others stay aboard and replace piston piston rod cylinder cover cross head and bolt with the aid of the faithful donkey engine. the cylinder cover be hardly steam proof and the eye of science might have see in the connect rod a flexure something like that of a christmas tree candle which ha melt and be straighten by hand over a stave but a mr. wardrop say she didn t hit anything. 
a soon a the last bolt be in place men tumble over one another in their anxiety to get to the hand start gear the wheel and worm by which some engine can be move when there be no steam aboard. they nearly wrench off the wheel but it be evident to the blind eye that the engine stir. they do not revolve in their orbit with any enthusiasm a good machine should. indeed they groan not a little. but they move over and come to rest in a way which prove that they still recognise man s hand. then mr. wardrop send his slave into the dark bowel of the engine room and the stoke hole and follow them with a flare lamp. the boiler be sound but would take no harm from a little scale and clean. mr. wardrop would not have any one over zealous for he fear what the next stroke of the tool might show. the le we know about her now say he the good for u all i m thinkin. ye ll understand me when i say that this be in no sense regular engineerin. 
a his raiment when he speak be his grey beard and uncut hair they believe him. they do not ask too much of what they meet but polish and tallowed and scrap it to a false brilliancy. 
a lick of paint would make me easy in my mind say mr. wardrop plaintively. i know half the condenser tube be start. and the propeller shaftin s god know how far out of the true and we ll need a new air pump an the main steam leak like a sieve and there s bad each way i look. but paint s like clothe to a man an ours be near all go. 
the skipper unearth some stale ropy paint of the loathsome green that they use for the galley of sail ship and mr. wardrop spread it abroad lavishly to give the engine self respect. 
his own be return day by day for he wear his loin cloth continuously. but the crew have work under order do not feel a he do. the complete work satisfy mr. wardrop. he would at the last have make shift to run to singapore and go home without vengeance take to show his engine to his brother in the craft. but the others and the captain forbid him. they have not yet recover their self respect. 
it would be safe to make what ye might call a trial trip but beggar mustn t be chooser. an if the engine will go over to the hand gear the probability i m only say it s a probability the chance be that they ll hold up when we put steam on her. 
how long will you take to get steam. say the skipper. 
god know. four hour a day half a week. if i can raise sixty pound i ll not complain. 
be sure of her first. we can t afford to go out half a mile and break down. 
my soul and body man we re one continuous breakdown fore an aft. we might fetch singapore though. 
we ll break down at pygang watai where we can do good be the answer in a voice that do not allow argument. she s my boat and i ve have eight month to think in. 
no man saw the haliotis depart though many hear her. she leave at two in the morning have cut her mooring and it be none of her crew s pleasure that the engine should strike up a thunder half sea over chanty that echo among the hill. mr. wardrop wipe away a tear a he listen to the new song. 
she s gibberin she s just gibberin he whimper. yon s the voice of a maniac. 
and if engine have any soul a their master believe he be quite right. there be outcry and clamour sob and burst of chatter laughter silence where the train ear yearn for the clear note and torture reduplication where there should have be one deep voice. down the screw shaft run murmur and warning while a heart diseased flutter without tell that the propeller need re key. 
how doe she make it. say the skipper. 
she move but but she s breakin my heart. the sooner we re at pygang watai the good. she s mad and we re wake the town. 
be she at all near safe. 
what do i care how safe she be. she s mad. hear that now. to be sure nothing s hittin anything and the bearin s be fairly cool but can ye not hear. 
if she go say the skipper i don t care a curse. and she s my boat too. 
she go trail a fathom of weed behind her. from a slow two knot an hour she crawl up to a triumphant four. anything beyond that make the strut quiver dangerously and fill the engine room with steam. morning show her out of sight of land and there be a visible ripple under her bow. but she complain bitterly in her bowel and a though the noise have call it there shoot along across the purple sea a swift dark proa hawk like and curious which presently range alongside and wish to know if the haliotis be helpless. ship even the steamer of the white men have be know to break down in those water and the honest malay and javanese trader would sometimes aid them in their own peculiar way. but this ship be not full of lady passenger and well dress officer. men white naked and savage swarm down her side some with red hot iron bar and others with large hammer throw themselves upon those innocent inquire stranger and before any man could say what have happen be in full possession of the proa while the lawful owner bob in the water overside. half an hour late the proa s cargo of sago and trepang a well a a doubtful mind compass be in the haliotis. the two huge triangular mat sail with their seventy foot yard and boom have follow the cargo and be be fit to the strip mast of the steamer. 
they rise they swell they fill and the empty steamer visibly lay over a the wind take them. they give her nearly three knot an hour and what good could men ask. but if she have be forlorn before this new purchase make her horrible to see. imagine a respectable charwoman in the tights of a ballet dancer roll drink along the street and you will come to some faint notion of the appearance of that nine hundred ton well deck once schooner rig cargo boat a she stagger under her new help shout and rave across the deep. with steam and sail that marvellous voyage continue. and the bright eye crew look over the rail desolate unkempt unshorn shamelessly clothe beyond the decency. 
at the end of the third week she sight the island of pygang watai whose harbour be the turn point of a pearl sea patrol. here the gun boat stay for a week ere they retrace their line. there be no village at pygang watai. only a stream of water some palm and a harbour safe to rest in till the first violence of the southeast monsoon ha blow itself out. 
they open up the low coral beach with it mound of whitewash coal ready for supply the desert hut for the sailor and the flagless flagstaff. 
next day there be no haliotis only a little proa rock in the warm rain at the mouth of the harbour whose crew watch with hungry eye the smoke of a gunboat on the horizon. 
month afterwards there be a few line in an english newspaper to the effect that some gunboat of some foreign power have break her back at the mouth of some far away harbour by run at full speed into a sink wreck.

martyn pick the pioneer from the table read through the telegram once more and put up his foot on the chair rest. it be a hot dark breathless even heavy with the smell of the newly water mall. the flower in the club garden be dead and black on their stalk the little lotus pond be a circle of cake mud and the tamarisk tree be white with the dust of week. most of the men be at the band stand in the public garden from the club verandah you could hear the native police band hammer stale waltz or on the polo grind or in the high wall five court hot than a dutch oven. half a dozen groom squat at the head of their pony wait their master return. from time to time a man would ride at a foot pace into the club compound and listlessly loaf over to the whitewash barrack beside the main build. these be suppose to be chamber. men live in them meet the same white face night after night at dinner and draw out their office work till the late possible hour that they might escape that doleful company. 
what be you go to do. say martyn with a yawn. let s have a swim before dinner. 
water s hot. i be at the bath to day. 
play you game o billiards fifty up. 
it s a hundred and five in the hall now. sit still and don t be so abominably energetic. 
a grunt camel swing up to the porch his badge and belt rider fumble a leather pouch. 
kubber kargaz ki yektraaa the man whine hand down the newspaper extra a slip print on one side only and damp from the press. it be pin up on the green baize board between notice of pony for sale and fox terrier miss.

good business. say scott with the first sign of interest he have show. when in doubt hire a punjabi. i work under jimmy when i first come out and he belong to the punjab. he ha more bundobust than most men. 
jimmy s a jubilee knight now say martyn. he s a good chap even though he be a thrice bear civilian and go to the benight presidency. what unholy name these madras district rejoice in all ungas or rungas or pillays or polliums. 
a dog cart drive up in the dusk and a man enter mop his head. he be editor of the one daily paper at the capital of a province of twenty five million native and a few hundred white men. a his staff be limit to himself and one assistant his office hour run variously from ten to twenty a day. 
hi rain. you re suppose to know everything say martyn stop him. how s this madras scarcity go to turn out. 
no one know a yet. there s a message a long a your arm come in on the telephone. i ve leave my cub to fill it out. madras ha own she can t manage it alone and jimmy seem to have a free hand in get all the men he need. arbuthnot s warn to hold himself in readiness.

scott move leisurely to his room and change into the even dress of the season and the country. spotless white linen from head to foot with a broad silk cummerbund. dinner at the martyns be a decide improvement on the goat mutton twiney tough fowl and tin entree of the club. but it be a great pity that martyn could not afford to send his sister to the hill for the hot weather. a an act district superintendent of police martyn draw the magnificent pay of six hundred depreciate silver rupee a month and his little four room bungalow say just a much. there be the usual blue and white strip jail make rug on the uneven floor. the usual glass stud amritsar phulkaris drape on nail drive into the flake whitewash of the wall. the usual half dozen chair that do not match pick up at sale of dead men s effect. and the usual streak of black grease where the leather punka thong run through the wall. it be a though everything have be unpack the night before to be repacked next morning. not a door in the house be true on it hinge. the little window fifteen foot up be darken with wasp nest and lizard hunt fly between the beam of the wood ceiled roof. but all this be part of scott s life. thus do people live who have such an income. and in a land where each man s pay age and position be print in a book that all may read it be hardly worth while to play at pretence in word or deed. scott count eight year service in the irrigation department and draw eight hundred rupee a month on the understand that if he serve the state faithfully for another twenty two year he could retire on a pension of some four hundred rupee a month. his work life which have be spend chiefly under canvas or in temporary shelter where a man could sleep eat and write letter be bind up with the open and guard of irrigation canal the handle of two or three thousand workman of all caste and creed and the payment of vast sum of coin silver. 
he have finish that spring not without credit the last section of the great mosuhl canal and much against his will for he hat office work have be send in to serve during the hot weather on the account and supply side of the department with sole charge of the swelter sub office at the capital of the province. martyn know this. william his sister know it. and everybody know it. scott know too a well a the rest of the world that miss martyn have come out to india four year ago to keep house for her brother who a every one know have borrow the money to pay for her passage and that she ought a all the world say to have marry at once. in stead of this she have refuse some half a dozen subaltern a civilian twenty year her senior one major and a man in the indian medical department. this too be common property. she have stay down three hot weather a the say be because her brother be in debt and could not afford the expense of her keep at even a cheap hill station. therefore her face be white a bone and in the centre of her forehead be a big silvery scar about the size of a shill the mark of a delhi sore which be the same a a bagdad date. this come from drink bad water and slowly eat into the flesh till it be ripe enough to be burn out. 
none the le william have enjoy herself hugely in her four year. twice she have be nearly drown while ford a river. once she have be run away with on a camel. have witness a midnight attack of thief on her brother s camp. have see justice administer with long stick in the open under tree. could speak urdu and even rough punjabi with a fluency that be envy by her senior. have entirely fall out of the habit of write to her aunt in england or cut the page of the english magazine. have be through a very bad cholera year see sight unfit to be tell. and have wind up her experience by six week of typhoid fever during which her head have be shave and hop to keep her twenty third birthday that september. it be conceivable that the aunt would not have approve of a girl who never set foot on the grind if a horse be within hail. who ride to dance with a shawl throw over her skirt. who wear her hair crop and curl all over her head. who answer indifferently to the name of william or bill. whose speech be heavy with the flower of the vernacular. who could act in amateur theatrical play on the banjo rule eight servant and two horse their account and their disease and look men slowly and deliberately between the eye even after they have propose to her and be reject. 
i like men who do thing she have confide to a man in the educational department who be teach the son of cloth merchant and dyer the beauty of wordsworth s excursion in annotate cram book. and when he grow poetical william explain that she didn t understand poetry very much. it make her head ache and another break heart take refuge at the club. but it be all william s fault. she delight in hear men talk of their own work and that be the most fatal way of bring a man to your foot. 
scott have know her for some three year meet her a a rule under canvas when his camp and her brother s join for a day on the edge of the indian desert. he have dance with her several time at the big christmas gathering when a many a five hundred white people come in to the station. and have always a great respect for her housekeep and her dinner. 
she look more like a boy than ever when the meal end she sit roll cigarette her low forehead pucker beneath the dark curl a she twiddle the paper and stick out her round chin when the tobacco stay in place or with a gesture a true a a school boy s throw a stone toss the finish article across the room to martyn who catch it with one hand and continue his talk with scott. it be all shop canal and the police of canal. the sin of villager who steal more water than they have pay for and the gross sin of native constable who connive at the theft. of the transplant bodily of village to newly irrigate grind and of the come fight with the desert in the south when the provincial fund should warrant the open of the long survey luni protective canal system. and scott speak openly of his great desire to be put on one particular section of the work where he know the land and the people. and martyn sigh for a billet in the himalayan foot hill and say his mind of his superior and william roll cigarette and say nothing but smile gravely on her brother because he be happy. 
at ten scott s horse come to the door and the even be end. the light of the two low bungalow in which the daily paper be print show bright across the road. it be too early to try to find sleep and scott drift over to the editor. rain strip to the waist like a sailor at a gun lay half asleep in a long chair wait for night telegram. he have a theory that if a man do not stay by his work all day and most of the night he lay himself open to fever. so he eat and sleep among his file.

a pink and fattish youth arrive in the red hot noonday whimper a little at fate and famine which never allow any one three month peace. he be scott s successor another cog in the machinery move forward behind his fellow whose service a the official announcement run be place at the disposal of the madras government for famine duty until further order. scott hand over the fund in his charge show him the cool corner in the office warn him against excess of zeal and a twilight fell depart from the club in a hire carriage with his faithful body servant faiz ullah and a mound of disorder baggage atop to catch the southern mail at the loopholed and bastioned railway station. the heat from the thick brick wall strike him across the face a if it have be a hot towel. and he reflect that there be at least five night and four day of this travel before him. faiz ullah use to the chance of service plunge into the crowd on the stone platform while scott a black cheroot between his teeth wait till his compartment should be set away. a dozen native policeman with their rifle and bundle shoulder into the press of punjabi farmer sikh craftsman and greasy lock afreedee pedlar escort with all pomp martyn s uniform case water bottle ice box and bed roll. they saw faiz ullah s lift hand and steer for it.

all the sister i ve ever hear of would have stay where they be well off. 
she s a clever a a man confound martyn go on. she break up the bungalow over my head while i be talk at her. settle the whole thing in three hour servant horse and all. i didn t get my order till nine. 
jimmy hawkins win t be please say scott a famine s no place for a woman. 
mr. jim i mean lady jim s in camp with him. at any rate she say she will look after my sister. william wire down to her on her own responsibility ask if she could come and knock the grind from under me by show me her answer. 
scott laugh aloud. if she can do that she can take care of herself and mr. jim win t let her run into any mischief. there aren t many woman sister or wife who would walk into a famine with their eye open. it isn t a if she didn t know what these thing mean. she be through the jalo cholera last year. 
the train stop at amritsar and scott go back to the lady compartment immediately behind their carriage. william with a cloth rid cap on her curl nod affably. 
come in and have some tea she say. best thing in the world for heat apoplexy. 
do i look a if i be go to have heat apoplexy. 
never can tell say william wisely. it s always best to be ready. 
she have arrange her compartment with the knowledge of an old campaigner. a felt cover water bottle hang in the draught of one of the shutter window. a tea set of russian china pack in a wad basket stand on the seat. and a travel spirit lamp be clamp against the woodwork above it. 
william serve them generously in large cup hot tea which save the vein of the neck from swell inopportunely on a hot night. it be characteristic of the girl that her plan of action once settle she ask for no comment on it. life among men who have a great deal of work to do and very little time to do it in have teach her the wisdom of efface a well a of fend for herself. she do not by word or deed suggest that she would be useful comfort or beautiful in their travel but continue about her business serenely. put the cup back without clatter when tea be end and make cigarette for her guest. 
this time last night say scott we didn t expect er this kind of thing do we. 
i ve learn to expect anything say william. you know in our service we live at the end of the telegraph. but of course this ought to be a good thing for u all departmentally if we live. 
it knock u out of the run in our own province scott reply with equal gravity. i hop to be put on the luni protective work this cold weather but there s no say how long the famine may keep u. 
hardly beyond october i should think say martyn. it will be end one way or the other then. 
and we ve nearly a week of this say william. sha n t we be dusty when it s over. 
for a night and a day they know their surround and for a night and a day skirt the edge of the great indian desert on a narrow gauge railway they remember how in the day of their apprenticeship they have come by that road from bombay. then the language in which the name of the station be write change and they launch south into a foreign land where the very smell be new. many long and heavily lade grain train be in front of them and they could feel the hand of jimmy hawkins from far off. they wait in extemporise siding while procession of empty truck return to the north and be couple on to slow crawl train and drop at midnight heaven know where. but it be furiously hot and they walk to and fro among sack and dog howl. then they come to an india more strange to them than to the untravelled englishman the flat red india of palm tree palmyra palm and rice the india of the picture book of little harry and his bearer all dead and dry in the bake heat. they have leave the incessant passenger traffic of the north and west far and far behind them. here the people crawl to the side of the train hold their little one in their arm. and a load truck would be leave behind the men and woman cluster round it like ant by spill honey. once in the twilight they saw on a dusty plain a regiment of little brown men each bear a body over his shoulder. and when the train stop to leave yet another truck they perceive that the burden be not corps but only foodless folk pick up beside dead ox by a corp of irregular troop. now they meet more white men here one and there two whose tent stand close to the line and who come arm with write authority and angry word to cut off a truck. they be too busy to do more than nod at scott and martyn and stare curiously at william who could do nothing except make tea and watch how her men stave off the rush of wail walk skeleton put them down three at a time in heap with their own hand uncouple the mark truck or take receipt from the hollow eye weary white men who speak another argot than theirs. they run out of ice out of soda water and out of tea. for they be six day and seven night on the road and it seem to them like seven time seven year. 
at last in a dry hot dawn in a land of death light by long red fire of railway sleeper where they be burn the dead they come to their destination and be meet by jim hawkins the head of the famine unshaven unwashed but cheery and entirely in command of affair. 
martyn he decree then and there be to live on train till further order. be to go back with empty truck fill them with starve people a he find them and drop them at a famine camp on the edge of the eight district. he would pick up supply and return and his constable would guard the load grain car also pick up people and would drop them at a camp a hundred mile south. scott hawkins be very glad to see scott again would that same hour take charge of a convoy of bullock cart and would go south feed a he go to yet another famine camp where he would leave his starve there would be no lack of starve on the route and wait for order by telegraph. generally scott be in all small thing to act a he think best. 
william bite her under lip. there be no one in the wide world like her one brother but martyn s order give him no discretion. 
she come out on the platform mask with dust from head to foot a horse shoe wrinkle on her forehead put here by much think during the past week but a self possess a ever. mr. jim who should have be lady jim but that no one remember the title take possession of her with a little gasp. 
oh i m so glad you re here she almost sob. you oughtn t to of course but there there isn t another woman in the place and we must help each other you know. and we ve all the wretched people and the little baby they be sell. 
i ve see some say william. 
isn t it ghastly. i ve buy twenty. they re in our camp. but win t you have something to eat first. we ve more than ten people can do here. and i ve get a horse for you. oh i m so glad you ve come dear. you re a punjabi too you know. 
steady lizzie say hawkins over his shoulder. we ll look after you miss martyn. sorry i can t ask you to breakfast martyn. you ll have to eat a you go. leave two of your men to help scott. these poor devil can t stand up to load cart. saunders. this to the engine driver who be half asleep in the cab. back down and get those empty away. you ve line clear to anundrapillay. they ll give you order north of that. scott load up your cart from that b. p. p. truck and be off a soon a you can. the eurasian in the pink shirt be your interpreter and guide. you ll find an apothecary of sort tie to the yoke of the second wagon. he s be try to bolt. you ll have to look after him. lizzie drive miss martyn to camp and tell them to send the red horse down here for me. 
scott with faiz ullah and two policeman be already busy with the cart back them up to the truck and unbolt the sideboard quietly while the others pitch in the bag of millet and wheat. hawkins watch him for a long a it take to fill one cart. 
that s a good man he say. if all go well i shall work him hard. this be jim hawkins s notion of the high compliment one human be could pay another. 
an hour late scott be under way. the apothecary threaten him with the penalty of the law for that he a member of the subordinate medical department have be coerce and bind against his will and all law govern the liberty of the subject. the pink shirt eurasian beg leave to see his mother who happen to be die some three mile away. only verree verree short leave of absence and will presently return sar. the two constable arm with stave bring up the rear. and faiz ullah a mohammedan s contempt for all hindoo and foreigner in every line of his face explain to the driver that though scott sahib be a man to be fear on all four he faiz ullah be authority itself. 
the procession creak past hawkins s camp three stain tent under a clump of dead tree behind them the famine shed where a crowd of hopeless one toss their arm around the cook kettle. 
wish to heaven william have keep out of it say scott to himself after a glance. we ll have cholera sure a a gun when the rain break. 
but william seem to have take kindly to the operation of the famine code which when famine be declare supersede the working of the ordinary law. scott saw her the centre of a mob of weep woman in a calico rid habit and a blue grey felt hat with a gold puggaree. 
i want fifty rupee please. i forget to ask jack before he go away. can you lend it me. it s for condense milk for the baby say she. 
scott take the money from his belt and hand it over without a word. for goodness sake take care of yourself he say. 
oh i shall be all right. we ought to get the milk in two day. by the way the order be i be to tell you that you re to take one of sir jim s horse. there s a grey cabuli here that i think would be just your style so i ve say you d take him. be that right. 
that s awfully good of you. we can t either of u talk much about style i be afraid. 
scott be in a weather stain drill shoot kit very white at the seam and a little fray at the wrist. william regard him thoughtfully from his pith helmet to his grease ankle boot. you look very nice i think. be you sure you ve everything you ll need quinine chlorodyne and so on. 
think so say scott pat three or four of his shoot pocket a he mount and ride alongside his convoy. 
good bye he cry. 
good bye and good luck say william. i m awfully oblige for the money. she turn on a spur heel and disappear into the tent while the cart push on past the famine shed past the roar line of the thick fat fire down to the bake gehenna of the south. 
part ii. 
so let u melt and make no noise no tear flood nor sigh tempest move. twere profanation of our joy to tell the laity our love. 
a valediction. 
it be punish work even though he travel by night and camp by day. but within the limit of his vision there be no man whom scott could call master. he be a free a jimmy hawkins free in fact for the government hold the head of the famine tie neatly to a telegraph wire and if jimmy have ever regard telegram seriously the death rate of that famine would have be much high than it be. 
at the end of a few day crawl scott learn something of the size of the india which he serve and it astonish him. his cart a you know be load with wheat millet and barley good food grain need only a little grind. but the people to whom he bring the life give stuff be rice eater. they could hull rice in their mortar but they know nothing of the heavy stone quern of the north and le of the material that the white man convoy so laboriously. they clamour for rice unhusked paddy such a they be accustom to and when they find that there be none break away weep from the side of the cart. what be the use of these strange hard grain that choke their throat. they would die. and then and there very many of them keep their word. others take their allowance and barter enough millet to fee a man through a week for a few handful of rotten rice save by some le unfortunate. a few put their share into the rice mortar pound it and make a paste with foul water. but they be very few. scott understand dimly that many people in the india of the south eat rice a a rule but he have spend his service in a grain province have seldom see rice in the blade or ear and least of all would have believe that in time of deadly need men could die at arm s length of plenty sooner than touch food they do not know. in vain the interpreter interpret. in vain his two policeman show in vigorous pantomime what should be do. the starve creep away to their bark and weed grub leaf and clay and leave the open sack untouched. but sometimes the woman lay their phantom of child at scott s foot look back a they stagger away. 
faiz ullah opine it be the will of god that these foreigner should die and it remain only to give order to burn the dead. none the le there be no reason why the sahib should lack his comfort and faiz ullah a campaigner of experience have pick up a few lean goat and have add them to the procession. that they might give milk for the morning meal he be feed them on the good grain that these imbecile reject. yes say faiz ullah. if the sahib think fit a little milk might be give to some of the baby. but a the sahib well know baby be cheap and for his own part faiz ullah hold that there be no government order a to baby. scott speak forcefully to faiz ullah and the two policeman and bid them capture goat where they could find them. this they most joyfully do for it be a recreation and many ownerless goat be drive in. once feed the poor brute be will enough to follow the cart and a few day good food food such a human being die for lack of set them in milk again. 
but i be no goatherd say faiz ullah. it be against my izzat [my honour]. 
when we cross the bias river again we will talk of izzat scott reply. till that day thou and the policeman shall be sweeper to the camp if i give the order. 
thus then it be do grunt faiz ullah if the sahib will have it so. and he show how a goat should be milk while scott stand over him. 
now we will fee them say scott. twice a day we will fee them. and he bow his back to the milk and take a horrible cramp. 
when you have to keep connection unbroken between a restless mother of kid and a baby who be at the point of death you suffer in all your system. but the baby be feed. each morning and even scott would solemnly lift them out one by one from their nest of gunny bag under the cart tilt. there be always many who could do no more than breathe and the milk be drop into their toothless mouth drop by drop with due pause when they choke. each morning too the goat be feed. and since they would straggle without a leader and since the native be hireling scott be force to give up rid and pace slowly at the head of his flock accommodate his step to their weakness. all this be sufficiently absurd and he felt the absurdity keenly. but at least he be save life and when the woman saw that their child do not die they make shift to eat a little of the strange food and crawl after the cart bless the master of the goat. 
give the woman something to live for say scott to himself a he sneeze in the dust of a hundred little foot and they ll hang on somehow. this beat william s condense milk trick all to piece. i shall never live it down though. 
he reach his destination very slowly find that a rice ship have come in from burmah and that store of paddy be available. find also an overwork englishman in charge of the shed and load the cart set back to cover the grind he have already pass. he leave some of the child and half his goat at the famine shed. for this he be not thank by the englishman who have already more stray baby than he know what to do with. scott s back be supple to stoop now and he go on with his wayside ministration in addition to distribute the paddy. more baby and more goat be add unto him. but now some of the baby wear rag and bead round their wrist or neck. that say the interpreter a though scott do not know signify that their mother hope in eventual contingency to resume them offeecially. 
the sooner the good say scott. but at the same time he mark with the pride of ownership how this or that little ramasawmy be put on flesh like a bantam. a the paddy cart be empty he head for hawkins s camp by the railway time his arrival to fit in with the dinner hour for it be long since he have eat at a cloth. he have no desire to make any dramatic entry but an accident of the sunset order it that when he have take off his helmet to get the even breeze the low light should fall across his forehead and he could not see what be before him. while one wait at the tent door behold with new eye a young man beautiful a paris a god in a halo of golden dust walk slowly at the head of his flock while at his knee run small naked cupid. but she laugh william in a slate colour blouse laugh consumedly till scott put the best face he could upon the matter halt his army and bid her admire the kindergarten. it be an unseemly sight but the propriety have be leave age ago with the tea party at amritsar station fifteen hundred mile to the north. 
they be come on nicely say william. we ve only five and twenty here now. the woman be begin to take them away again. 
be you in charge of the baby then. 
yes mr. jim and i. we didn t think of goat though. we ve be try condense milk and water. 
any loss. 
more than i care to think of. say william with a shudder. and you. 
scott say nothing. there have be many little burial along his route one cannot burn a dead baby many mother who have weep when they do not find again the child they have trust to the care of the government. 
then hawkins come out carry a razor at which scott look hungrily for he have a beard that he do not love. and when they sit down to dinner in the tent he tell his tale in few word a it might have be an official report. mr. jim snuffle from time to time and jim bow his head judicially. but william s grey eye be on the clean shave face and it be to her that scott seem to appeal. 
good for the pauper province. say william her chin on her hand a she lean forward among the wine glass. her cheek have fall in and the scar on her forehead be more prominent than ever but the well turn neck rise roundly a a column from the ruffle of the blouse which be the accept even dress in camp.

he s just the least bite in the world tuck up say jim to himself but he can do two men s work yet. then he be aware that mr. jim be telegraph to him and accord to the domestic code the message run. a clear case. look at them. 
he look and listen. all that william be say be. what can you expect of a country where they call a bhistee [a water carrier] a tunni cutch. and all that scott answer be. i shall be glad to get back to the club. save me a dance at the christmas ball win t you. 
it s a far cry from here to the lawrence hall say jim. good turn in early scott. it s paddy cart to morrow. you ll begin load at five. 
aren t you go to give mr. scott a single day s rest. 
wish i could lizzie but i m afraid i can t. a long a he can stand up we must use him. 
well i ve have one europe even at least. by jove i d nearly forget. what do i do about those baby of mine.

you forget i ve have some experience here. 
i hope to goodness you win t overdo. scott s voice be unguarded. 
i ll take care of her say mr. jim telegraph hundred word message a she carry william off. while jim give scott his order for the come campaign. it be very late nearly nine o clock.

not a bite of it dear. i remember do the first jandiala settlement for the sake of a girl in a crinoline and she be slender lizzie. i ve never do a good a piece of work since. he ll work like a demon. 
but you might have give him one day. 
and let thing come to a head now. no dear. it s their happy time.

she s a darling. she ha do more work under me. 
under you. the day after she come she be in charge and you be her subordinate. you ve stay there ever since. she manage you almost a well a you manage me.

the talk end. far away in the derajat be a child s grave more than twenty year old and neither jim nor his wife speak of it any more.

bless em. say mr. jim sleepily. 
before the star pal scott who sleep in an empty cart wake and go about his work in silence. it seem at that hour unkind to rouse faiz ullah and the interpreter. his head be close to the grind he do not hear william till she stand over him in the dingy old rid habit her eye still heavy with sleep a cup of tea and a piece of toast in her hand. there be a baby on the grind squirm on a piece of blanket and a six year old child peer over scott s shoulder.

a cool white hand steady the brat who forthwith choke a the milk gurgle into his mouth.

yes. it be absurd. now you try he say give place to the girl. look out. a goat s not a cow.

that be the custom of the sahib when truth be tell in their presence say faiz ullah. the time come that i must seek new service. young wife especially such a speak our language and have knowledge of the way of the police make great trouble for honest butler in the matter of weekly account. 
what william think of it all she do not say but when her brother ten day late come to camp for order and hear of scott s performance he say laugh. well that settle it. he ll be bakri scott to the end of his day. bakri in the northern vernacular mean a goat. what a lark. i d have give a month s pay to have see him nurse famine baby. i feed some with conjee [rice water] but that be all right. 
it s perfectly disgust say his sister with blaze eye. a man doe something like like that and all you other men think of be to give him an absurd nickname and then you laugh and think it s funny. 
ah say mr. jim sympathetically.

when he return to his duty on the railway martyn spread the name far and wide among his associate so that scott meet it a he lead his paddy cart to war. the native believe it to be some english title of honour and the cart driver use it in all simplicity till faiz ullah who do not approve of foreign jape break their head. there be very little time for milk now except at the big camp where jim have extend scott s idea and be feed large flock on the useless northern grain. sufficient paddy have come now into the eight district to hold the people safe if it be only distribute quickly and for that purpose no one be good than the big canal officer who never lose his temper never give an unnecessary order and never question an order give. scott press on save his cattle wash their gall neck daily so that no time should be lose on the road. report himself with his rice at the minor famine shed unload and go back light by force night march to the next distribute centre to find hawkins s unvarying telegram. do it again. and he do it again and again and yet again while jim hawkins fifty mile away mark off on a big map the track of his wheel gridironing the stricken land. others do well hawkins report at the end they all do well but scott be the most excellent for he keep good coin rupee by him settle for his own cart repair on the spot and run to meet all sort of unconsidered extra trust to be recoup late on. theoretically the government should have pay for every shoe and linchpin for every hand employ in the load. but government voucher cash themselves slowly and intelligent and efficient clerk write at great length contest unauthorised expenditure of eight anna. the man who want to make his work a success must draw on his own bank account of money or other thing a he go. 
i tell you he d work say jimmy to his wife at the end of six week. he s be in sole charge of a couple of thousand men up north on the mosuhl canal for a year. but he give le trouble than young martyn with his ten constable. and i m morally certain only government doesn t recognise moral obligation he s spend about half his pay to grease his wheel. look at this lizzie for one week s work. forty mile in two day with twelve cart. two day halt build a famine shed for young rogers. rogers ought to have build it himself the idiot. then forty mile back again load six cart on the way and distribute all sunday. then in the even he pitch in a twenty page demi official to me say the people where he be might be advantageously employ on relief work and suggest that he put em to work on some break down old reservoir he s discover so a to have a good water supply when the rain break. think he can cauk the dam in a fortnight. look at his marginal sketch aren t they clear and good. i know he be pukka but i didn t know he be a pukka a this. 
i must show these to william say mr. jim. the child s wear herself out among the baby. 
not more than you be dear. well another two month ought to see u out of the wood. i m sorry it s not in my power to recommend you for a v. c. 
william sit late in her tent that night read through page after page of the square handwrite pat the sketch of propose repair to the reservoir and wrinkle her eyebrow over the column of figure of estimate water supply. and he find time to do all this she cry to herself and well i also be present. i ve save one or two baby. 
she dream for the twentieth time of the god in the golden dust and wake refresh to fee loathsome black child score of them wastrel pick up by the wayside their bone almost break their skin terrible and cover with sore. 
scott be not allow to leave his cart work but his letter be duly forward to the government and he have the consolation not rare in india of know that another man be reap where he have sow. that also be discipline profitable to the soul. 
he s much too good to waste on canal say jimmy. any one can oversee cooly. you needn t be angry william. he can but i need my pearl among bullock driver and i ve transfer him to the khanda district where he ll have it all to do over again. he should be march now. 
he s not a coolie say william furiously. he ought to be do his regulation work. 
he s the best man in his service and that s say a good deal. but if you must use razor to cut grindstone why i prefer the best cutlery. 
isn t it almost time we saw him again. say mr. jim. i m sure the poor boy hasn t have a respectable meal for a month. he probably sit on a cart and eat sardine with his finger. 
all in good time dear. duty before decency wasn t it mr. chuck say that. 
no. it be midshipman easy william laugh. i sometimes wonder how it will feel to dance or listen to a band again or sit under a roof. i can t believe i ever wear a ball frock in my life.

how do you know dear.

one certainly get to know people rather well in time like these say jim drily. but william s face be serene a ever and even a she prophesy scott do not appear. 
the rain fell at last late but heavily. and the dry gash earth be red mud and servant kill snake in the camp where every one be weather bind for a fortnight all except hawkins who take horse and plash about in the wet rejoice. now the government decree that seed grain should be distribute to the people a well a advance of money for the purchase of new ox. and the white men be doubly work for this new duty while william skip from brick to brick lay down on the trample mud and dose her charge with warm medicine that make them rub their little round stomach. and the milch goat thrive on the rank grass. there be never a word from scott in the khanda district away to the southeast except the regular telegraphic report to hawkins. the rude country road have disappear. his driver be half mutinous. one of martyn s loan policeman have die of cholera. and scott be take thirty grain of quinine a day to fight the fever that come with the rain. but those be thing scott do not consider necessary to report. he be a usual work from a base of supply on a railway line to cover a circle of fifteen mile radius and since full load be impossible he take quarter load and toil four time a hard by consequence. for he do not choose to risk an epidemic which might have grow uncontrollable by assemble villager in thousand at the relief shed. it be cheap to take government bullock work them to death and leave them to the crow in the wayside slough. 
that be the time when eight year of clean live and hard condition tell though a man s head be ring like a bell from the cinchona and the earth sway under his foot when he stand and under his bed when he sleep. if hawkins have see fit to make him a bullock driver that he think be entirely hawkins s own affair. there be men in the north who would know what he have do. men of thirty year service in his own department who would say that it be not half bad. and above immeasurably above all men of all grade there be william in the thick of the fight who would approve because she understand. he have so train his mind that it would hold fast to the mechanical routine of the day though his own voice sound strange in his own ear and his hand when he write grow large a pillow or small a pea at the end of his wrist. that steadfastness bore his body to the telegraph office at the railway station and dictate a telegram to hawkins say that the khanda district be in his judgment now safe and he wait further order. 
the madrassee telegraph clerk do not approve of a large gaunt man fall over him in a dead faint not so much because of the weight a because of the name and blow that faiz ullah deal him when he find the body roll under a bench. then faiz ullah take blanket quilt and coverlet where he find them and lay down under them at his master s side and bind his arm with a tent rope and fill him with a horrible stew of herb and set the policeman to fight him when he wish to escape from the intolerable heat of his covering and shut the door of the telegraph office to keep out the curious for two night and one day. and when a light engine come down the line and hawkins kick in the door scott hail him weakly but in a natural voice and faiz ullah stand back and take all the credit. 
for two night heaven bear he be pagal say faiz ullah. look at my nose and consider the eye of the policeman. he beat u with his bind hand. but we sit upon him heaven bear and though his word be tez we sweat him. heaven bear never ha be such a sweat. he be weak now than a child. but the fever ha go out of him by the grace of god. there remain only my nose and the eye of the constabeel. sahib shall i ask for my dismissal because my sahib ha beat me. and faiz ullah lay his long thin hand carefully on scott s chest to be sure that the fever be all go ere he go out to open tin soup and discourage such a laugh at his swell nose.

morning bring the penetrate chill of the northern december the layer of wood smoke the dusty grey blue of the tamarisk the dome of ruin tomb and all the smell of the white northern plain a the mail train run on to the mile long sutlej bridge. william wrap in a poshteen a silk embroider sheepskin jacket trim with rough astrakhan look out with moist eye and nostril that dilate joyously. the south of pagoda and palm tree the overpopulate hindu south be do with. here be the land she know and love and before her lay the good life she understand among folk of her own caste and mind. 
they be pick them up at almost every station now men and woman come in for the christmas week with racquet with bundle of polo stick with dear and bruise cricket bat with fox terrier and saddle. the great part of them wear jacket like william s for the northern cold be a little to be trifle with a the northern heat. and william be among them and of them her hand deep in her pocket her collar turn up over her ear stamp her foot on the platform a she walk up and down to get warm visit from carriage to carriage and everywhere be congratulate. scott be with the bachelor at the far end of the train where they chaff him mercilessly about feed baby and milk goat. but from time to time he would stroll up to william s window and murmur. good enough isn t it. and william would answer with sigh of pure delight. good enough indeed. the large open name of the home town be good to listen to. umballa ludianah phillour jullundur they ring like the come marriage bell in her ear and william felt deeply and truly sorry for all stranger and outsider visitor tourist and those fresh catch for the service of the country. 
it be a glorious return and when the bachelor give the christmas ball william be unofficially you might say the chief and honour guest among the steward who could make thing very pleasant for their friend. she and scott dance nearly all the dance together and sit out the rest in the big dark gallery overlook the superb teak floor where the uniform blaze and the spur clink and the new frock and four hundred dancer go round and round till the drape flag on the pillar flap and belly to the whirl of it.

the maltese cat. 
they have good reason to be proud and good reason to be afraid all twelve of them. for though they have fight their way game by game up the team enter for the polo tournament they be meet the archangel that afternoon in the final match. and the archangel men be play with half a dozen pony apiece. a the game be divide into six quarter of eight minute each that mean a fresh pony after every halt. the skidars team even suppose there be no accident could only supply one pony for every other change. and two to one be heavy odds. again a shiraz the grey syrian point out they be meet the pink and pick of the polo pony of upper india pony that have cost from a thousand rupee each while they themselves be a cheap lot gather often from country cart by their master who belong to a poor but honest native infantry regiment. 
money mean pace and weight say shiraz rub his black silk nose dolefully along his neat fit boot and by the maxim of the game a i know it. 
ah but we aren t play the maxim say the maltese cat. we re play the game. and we ve the great advantage of know the game. just think a stride shiraz. we ve pull up from bottom to second place in two week against all those fellow on the grind here. that s because we play with our head a well a our foot. 
it make me feel undersized and unhappy all the same say kittiwynk a mouse colour mare with a red brow band and the clean pair of leg that ever an age pony own. they ve twice our style these others. 
kittiwynk look at the gather and sigh. the hard dusty polo grind be line with thousand of soldier black and white not count hundred and hundred of carriage and drag and dogcart and lady with brilliant colour parasol and officer in uniform and out of it and crowd of native behind them. and orderly on camel who have halt to watch the game instead of carry letter up and down the station. and native horse dealer run about on thin eared biluchi mare look for a chance to sell a few first class polo pony. then there be the pony of thirty team that have enter for the upper india free for all cup nearly every pony of worth and dignity from mhow to peshawar from allahabad to multan. prize pony arab syrian barb country breed deccanee waziri and kabul pony of every colour and shape and temper that you could imagine. some of them be in mat roof stable close to the polo grind but most be under saddle while their master who have be defeat in the early game trot in and out and tell the world exactly how the game should be play. 
it be a glorious sight and the come and go of the little quick hoof and the incessant salutation of pony that have meet before on other polo ground or race course be enough to drive a four foot thing wild. 
but the skidars team be careful not to know their neighbour though half the pony on the grind be anxious to scrape acquaintance with the little fellow that have come from the north and so far have sweep the board. 
let s see say a soft gold colour arab who have be play very badly the day before to the maltese cat. didn t we meet in abdul rahman s stable in bombay four season ago. i win the paikpattan cup next season you may remember. 
not me say the maltese cat politely. i be at malta then pull a vegetable cart. i don t race. i play the game. 
oh. say the arab cock his tail and swagger off. 
keep yourselves to yourselves say the maltese cat to his companion. we don t want to rub nose with all those goose rumped half breed of upper india. when we ve win this cup they ll give their shoe to know u. 
we sha n t win the cup say shiraz. how do you feel. 
stale a last night s fee when a muskrat ha run over it say polaris a rather heavy shoulder grey. and the rest of the team agree with him. 
the sooner you forget that the good say the maltese cat cheerfully. they ve finish tiffin in the big tent. we shall be want now. if your saddle be not comfy kick. if your bit aren t easy rear and let the saises know whether your boot be tight. 
each pony have his sais his groom who live and eat and sleep with the animal and have bet a good deal more than he could afford on the result of the game. there be no chance of anything go wrong but to make sure each sais be shampoo the leg of his pony to the last minute. behind the saises sit a many of the skidars regiment a have leave to attend the match about half the native officer and a hundred or two dark black beard men with the regimental piper nervously finger the big beribboned bagpipe. the skidars be what they call a pioneer regiment and the bagpipe make the national music of half their men. the native officer hold bundle of polo stick long cane handle mallet and a the grand stand fill after lunch they arrange themselves by one and two at different point round the grind so that if a stick be break the player would not have far to ride for a new one. an impatient british cavalry band strike up if you want to know the time ask a p leeceman. and the two umpire in light dust coat dance out on two little excite pony. the four player of the archangel team follow and the sight of their beautiful mount make shiraz groan again. 
wait till we know say the maltese cat. two of em be play in blinker and that mean they can t see to get out of the way of their own side or they may shy at the umpire pony. they ve all get white web rein that be sure to stretch or slip. 
and say kittiwynk dance to take the stiffness out of her they carry their whip in their hand instead of on their wrist. hah. 
true enough. no man can manage his stick and his rein and his whip that way say the maltese cat. i ve fall over every square yard of the malta grind and i ought to know. 
he quiver his little flea bite wither just to show how satisfy he felt. but his heart be not so light. ever since he have drift into india on a troop ship take with an old rifle a part payment for a race debt the maltese cat have play and preach polo to the skidars team on the skidars stony pologround. now a polo pony be like a poet. if he be bear with a love for the game he can be make. the maltese cat know that bamboo grow solely in order that poloballs might be turn from their root that grain be give to pony to keep them in hard condition and that pony be shoe to prevent them slip on a turn. but besides all these thing he know every trick and device of the fine game in the world and for two season have be teach the others all he know or guess. 
remember he say for the hundredth time a the rider come up you must play together and you must play with your head. whatever happen follow the ball. who go out first.

pull out to the leave say kittiwynk between her teeth. it s come your way cork. 
the back and half back of the archangel be tear down on her just a she be within reach of the ball. hughes lean forward with a loose rein and cut it away to the leave almost under kittiwynk s foot and it hop and skip off to cork who saw that if he be not quick it would run beyond the boundary. that long bounce drive give the archangel time to wheel and send three men across the grind to head off cork. kittiwynk stay where she be. for she know the game. cork be on the ball half a fraction of a second before the others come up and macnamara with a backhand stroke send it back across the grind to hughes who saw the way clear to the archangel goal and smack the ball in before any one quite know what have happen. 
that s luck say cork a they change end. a goal in three minute for three hit and no rid to speak of.

the third quarter of a game be generally the hot for each side think that the others must be pump. and most of the win play in a game be make about that time. 
lutyens take over the maltese cat with a pat and a hug for lutyens value him more than anything else in the world. powell have shikast a little grey rat with no pedigree and no manner outside polo. macnamara mount bamboo the large of the team. and hughes who s who alias the animal. he be suppose to have australian blood in his vein but he look like a clothe horse and you could whack his leg with an iron crow bar without hurt him.

who say anything about bite. i m not play tiddly wink. i m play the game. 
the archangel come down like a wolf on the fold for they be tire of football and they want polo. they get it more and more. just after the game begin lutyens hit a ball that be come towards him rapidly and it roll in the air a a ball sometimes will with the whirl of a frighten partridge. shikast hear but could not see it for the minute though he look everywhere and up into the air a the maltese cat have teach him. when he saw it ahead and overhead he go forward with powell a fast a he could put foot to grind. it be then that powell a quiet and level head man a a rule become inspire and play a stroke that sometimes come off successfully after long practice. he take his stick in both hand and stand up in his stirrup swipe at the ball in the air munipore fashion. there be one second of paralyse astonishment and then all four side of the grind go up in a yell of applause and delight a the ball fly true. you could see the amaze archangel duck in their saddle to dodge the line of flight and look at it with open mouth. and the regimental pipe of the skidars squeal from the railing a long a the piper have breath. shikast hear the stroke. but he hear the head of the stick fly off at the same time. nine hundred and ninety nine pony out of a thousand would have go tear on after the ball with a useless player pull at their head. but powell know him and he know powell. and the instant he felt powell s right leg shift a trifle on the saddle flap he head to the boundary where a native officer be frantically wave a new stick. before the shout have end powell be arm again. 
once before in his life the maltese cat have hear that very same stroke play off his own back and have profit by the confusion it work. this time he act on experience and leave bamboo to guard the goal in case of accident come through the others like a flash head and tail low lutyens stand up to ease him sweep on and on before the other side know what be the matter and nearly pitch on his head between the archangel goal post a lutyens kick the ball in after a straight scurry of a hundred and fifty yard. if there be one thing more than another upon which the maltese cat pride himself it be on this quick streak kind of run half across the grind. he do not believe in take ball round the field unless you be clearly overmatched. after this they give the archangel five minuted football. and an expensive fast pony hate football because it rumple his temper. who s who show himself even good than polaris in this game. he do not permit any wriggle away but bore joyfully into the scrimmage a if he have his nose in a fee box and be look for something nice. little shikast jump on the ball the minute it get clear and every time an archangel pony follow it he find shikast stand over it ask what be the matter. 
if we can live through this quarter say the maltese cat i sha n t care. don t take it out of yourselves. let them do the lather. 
so the pony a their rider explain afterwards shut up. the archangel keep them tie fast in front of their goal but it cost the archangel pony all that be leave of their temper. and pony begin to kick and men begin to repeat compliment and they chop at the leg of who s who and he set his teeth and stay where he be and the dust stand up like a tree over the scrimmage until that hot quarter end. 
they find the pony very excite and confident when they go to their saises. and the maltese cat have to warn them that the bad of the game be come. 
now we be all go in for the second time say he and they be trot out fresh pony. you think you can gallop but you ll find you can t. and then you ll be sorry. 
but two goal to nothing be a halter long lead say kittiwynk prance. 
how long doe it take to get a goal. the maltese cat answer. for pity s sake don t run away with a notion that the game be half win just because we happen to be in luck now. they ll ride you into the grand stand if they can. you must not give em a chance. follow the ball. 
football a usual. say polaris. my hock s half a big a a nose bag. 
don t let them have a look at the ball if you can help it. now leave me alone. i must get all the rest i can before the last quarter. 
he hang down his head and let all his muscle go slack shikast bamboo and who s who copy his example. 
good not watch the game he say. we aren t play and we shall only take it out of ourselves if we grow anxious. look at the grind and pretend it s fly time. 
they do their best but it be hard advice to follow. the hoof be drum and the stick be rattle all up and down the grind and yell of applause from the english troop tell that the archangel be press the skidars hard. the native soldier behind the pony groan and grunt and say thing in undertone and presently they hear a long draw shout and a clatter of hurrah.

the saises look at each other gravely a they rub their pony leg. this be the time when long purse begin to tell and everybody know it. kittiwynk and the others come back the sweat drip over their hoof and their tail tell sad story.

yes. but it s two arab and two country breds to play now say cork. faiz ullah remember. he speak in a bite voice. 
a lutyens mount grey dawn he look at his men and they do not look pretty. they be cover with dust and sweat in streak. their yellow boot be almost black their wrist be red and lumpy and their eye seem two inch deep in their head. but the expression in the eye be satisfactory.

all right. the archangel do. they be bad pump than we be.

that fifth quarter be a painful one in every way. faiz ullah play like a little red demon and the rabbit seem to be everywhere at once and benami ride straight at anything and everything that come in his way. while the umpire on their pony wheel like gull outside the shift game. but the archangel have the good mount they have keep their racer till late in the game and never allow the skidars to play football. they hit the ball up and down the width of the grind till benami and the rest be outpace. then they go forward and time and again lutyens and grey dawn be just and only just able to send the ball away with a long spit backhand. grey dawn forget that he be an arab. and turn from grey to blue a he gallop. indeed he forget too well for he do not keep his eye on the grind a an arab should but stick out his nose and scuttle for the dear honour of the game. they have water the grind once or twice between the quarter and a careless waterman have empty the last of his skinful all in one place near the skidars goal. it be close to the end of the play and for the tenth time grey dawn be bolt after the ball when his near hind foot slip on the greasy mud and he roll over and over pitch lutyens just clear of the goal post. and the triumphant archangel make their goal. then time be call two goal all. but lutyens have to be help up and grey dawn rise with his near hind leg strain somewhere. 
what s the damage. say powell his arm around lutyens.

and now say the maltese cat a they take their place remember that this be the last quarter and follow the ball. 
don t need to be tell say who s who. 
let me go on. all those people on all four side will begin to crowd in just a they do at malta. you ll hear people call out and move forward and be push back. and that be go to make the archangel pony very unhappy. but if a ball be strike to the boundary you go after it and let the people get out of your way. i go over the pole of a four in hand once and pick a game out of the dust by it. back me up when i run and follow the ball. 
there be a sort of an all round sound of sympathy and wonder a the last quarter open and then there begin exactly what the maltese cat have foresee. people crowd in close to the boundary and the archangel pony keep look sideways at the narrow space. if you know how a man feel to be cramp at tennis not because he want to run out of the court but because he like to know that he can at a pinch you will guess how pony must feel when they be play in a box of human being. 
i ll bend some of those men if i can get away say who s who a he rocket behind the ball. and bamboo nod without speak. they be play the last ounce in them and the maltese cat have leave the goal undefended to join them. lutyens give him every order that he could to bring him back but this be the first time in his career that the little wise grey have ever play polo on his own responsibility and he be go to make the most of it. 
what be you do here. say hughes a the cat cross in front of him and ride off an archangel. 
the cat s in charge mind the goal. shout lutyens and bow forward hit the ball full and follow on force the archangel towards their own goal. 
no football say the maltese cat. keep the ball by the boundary and cramp em. play open order and drive em to the boundary. 
across and across the grind in big diagonal fly the ball and whenever it come to a fly rush and a stroke close to the boundary the archangel pony move stiffly. they do not care to go headlong at a wall of men and carriage though if the grind have be open they could have turn on a sixpence. 
wriggle her up the side say the cat. keep her close to the crowd. they hate the carriage. shikast keep her up this side. 
shikast and powell lay leave and right behind the uneasy scuffle of an open scrimmage and every time the ball be hit away shikast gallop on it at such an angle that powell be force to hit it towards the boundary. and when the crowd have be drive away from that side lutyens would send the ball over to the other and shikast would slide desperately after it till his friend come down to help. it be billiards and no football this time billiards in a corner pocket. and the cue be not well chalk. 
if they get u out in the middle of the grind they ll walk away from u. dribble her along the side cry the maltese cat. 
so they dribble all along the boundary where a pony could not come on their right hand side. and the archangel be furious and the umpire have to neglect the game to shout at the people to get back and several blunder mount policeman try to restore order all close to the scrimmage and the nerve of the archangel pony stretch and break like cob web. 
five or six time an archangel hit the ball up into the middle of the grind and each time the watchful shikast give powell his chance to send it back and after each return when the dust have settle men could see that the skidars have gain a few yard.
