bread upon the water. 
if you remember my improper friend brugglesmith you will also bear in mind his friend mcphee chief engineer of the breslau whose dingey brugglesmith try to steal. his apology for the performance of brugglesmith may one day be tell in their proper place. the tale before u concern mcphee. he be never a race engineer and take special pride in say a much before the liverpool men. but he have a thirty two year knowledge of machinery and the humour of ship. one side of his face have be wreck through the burst of a pressure gauge in the day when men know le than they do now and his nose rise grandly out of the wreck like a club in a public riot. there be cut and lump on his head and he would guide your forefinger through his short iron grey hair and tell you how he have come by his trade mark. he own all sort of certificate of extra competency and at the bottom of his cabin chest of drawer where he keep the photograph of his wife be two or three royal humane society medal for save life at sea. professionally it be different when crazy steerage passenger jump overboard professionally mcphee doe not approve of save life at sea and he ha often tell me that a new hell await stoker and trimmer who sign for a strong man s pay and fall sick the second day out. he belief in throw boot at fourth and fifth engineer when they wake him up at night with word that a bear be redhot all because a lamp s glare be reflect red from the twirl metal. he belief that there be only two poet in the world. one be robert burn of course and the other gerald massey. when he ha time for novel he read wilkie collins and charles reade chiefly the latter and know whole page of very hard cash by heart. in the saloon his table be next to the captain s and he drink only water while his engine work. 
he be good to me when we first meet because i do not ask question and believe in charles reade a a most shamefully neglect author. late he approve of my writing to the extent of one pamphlet of twenty four page that i write for holdock steiner & chase owner of the line when they buy some ventilate patent and fit it to the cabin of the breslau spandau and koltzau. the purser of the breslau recommend me to holdock s secretary for the job. and holdock who be a wesleyan methodist invite me to his house and give me dinner with the govern when the others have finish and place the plan and specification in my hand and i write the pamphlet that same afternoon. it be call comfort in the cabin and bring me seven pound ten cash down an important sum of money in those day. and the govern who be teach master john holdock his scale tell me that mr. holdock have tell her to keep an eye on me in case i go away with coat from the hat rack. mcphee like that pamphlet enormously for it be compose in the bouverie byzantine style with baroque and rococo embellishment. and afterwards he introduce me to mr. mcphee who succeed dinah in my heart. for dinah be half a world away and it be wholesome and antiseptic to love such a woman a janet mcphee. they live in a little twelve pound house close to the ship. when mcphee be away mr. mcphee read the lloyd column in the paper and call on the wife of senior engineer of equal social stand. once or twice too mr. holdock visit mr. mcphee in a brougham with celluloid fitting and i have reason to believe that after she have play owner s wife long enough they talk scandal. the holdocks live in an old fashion house with a big brick garden not a mile from the mcphees for they stay by their money a their money stay by them. and in summer you meet their brougham solemnly junket by theydon bois or loughton. but i be mr. mcphee s friend for she allow me to convoy her westward sometimes to theatre where she sob or laugh or shiver with a simple heart. and she introduce me to a new world of doctor wife captain wife and engineer wife whose whole talk and think centre in and about ship and line of ship you have never hear of. there be sail ship with steward and mahogany and maple saloon trade to australia take cargo of consumptive and hopeless drunkard for whom a sea voyage be recommend. there be frowzy little west african boat full of rat and cockroach where men die anywhere but in their bunk. there be brazilian boat whose cabin could be hire for merchandise that go out load nearly awash. there be zanzibar and mauritius steamer and wonderful reconstruct boat that ply to the other tide of borneo. these be love and know for they earn our bread and a little butter and we despise the big atlantic boat and make fun of the p. & o. and orient liner and swear by our respective owner wesleyan baptist or presbyterian a the case might be. 
i have only just come back to england when mr. mcphee invite me to dinner at three o clock in the afternoon and the notepaper be almost bridal in it scent creaminess. when i reach the house i saw that there be new curtain in the window that must have cost forty five shilling a pair. and a mr. mcphee draw me into the little marble paper hall she look at me keenly and cry. 
have ye not hear. what d ye think o the hatrack. 
now that hat rack be oak thirty shilling at least. mcphee come down stair with a sober foot he step a lightly a a cat for all his weight when he be at sea and shake hand in a new and awful manner a parody of old holdock s style when he say good bye to his skipper. i perceive at once that a legacy have come to him but i hold my peace though mr. mcphee beg me every thirty second to eat a great deal and say nothing. it be rather a mad sort of meal because mcphee and his wife take hold of hand like little child. they always do after voyage. and nod and wink and choke and gurgle and hardly eat a mouthful. 
a female servant come in and wait. though mr. mcphee have tell me time and again that she would thank no one to do her housework while she have her health. but this be a servant with a cap and i saw mr. mcphee swell and swell under her garance colour gown. there be no small free board to janet mcphee nor be garance any subdue tint. and with all this unexplained pride and glory in the air i felt like watch firework without know the festival. when the maid have remove the cloth she bring a pineapple that would have cost half a guinea at that season. only mcphee ha his own way of get such thing. and a canton china bowl of dry lichi and a glass plate of preserve ginger and a small jar of sacred and imperial chow chow that perfume the room. mcphee get it from a dutchman in java and i think he doctor it with liqueur. but the crown of the feast be some madeira of the kind you can only come by if you know the wine and the man. a little maize wrap fig of clot madeira cigar go with the wine and the rest be a pale blue smoky silence. janet in her splendour smile on u two and pat mcphee s hand. 
we ll drink say mcphee slowly rub his chin to the eternal damnation o holdock steiner & chase. 
of course i answer amen though i have make seven pound ten shilling out of the firm. mcphee s enemy be mine and i be drink his madeira. 
ye ve hear nothing. say janet. not a word not a whisper. 
not a word nor a whisper. on my word i have not. 
tell him mac say she. and that be another proof of janet s goodness and wifely love. a small woman would have babble first but janet be five foot nine in her stocking. 
we re rich say mcphee. i shake hand all round. 
we re damn rich he add. i shake hand all round a second time. 
i ll go to sea no more unless there s no sayin a private yacht maybe wi a small an handy auxiliary. 
it s not enough for that say janet. we re fair rich well to do but no more. a new gown for church and one for the theatre. we ll have it make west. 
how much be it. i ask. 
twenty five thousand pound. i draw a long breath. an i ve be earnin twenty five an twenty pound a month. 
the last word come away with a roar a though the wide world be conspire to beat him down. 
all this time i m wait i say. i know nothing since last september. be it leave you. 
they laugh aloud together. it be leave say mcphee choke. ou ay it be leave. that s vara good. of course it be leave. janet d ye note that. it be leave. now if you d put that in your pamphlet it would have be vara jocose. it be leave. he slap his thigh and roar till the wine quiver in the decanter. 
the scotch be a great people but they be apt to hang over a joke too long particularly when no one can see the point but themselves. 
when i rewrite my pamphlet i ll put it in mcphee. only i must know something more first. 
mcphee think for the length of half a cigar while janet catch my eye and lead it round the room to one new thing after another the new vine pattern carpet the new chime rustic clock between the model of the colombo outrigger boat the new inlay sideboard with a purple cut glass flower stand the fender of gild and brass and last the new black and gold piano. 
in october o last year the board sack me begin mcphee. in october o last year the breslau come in for winter overhaul. she d be runnin eight month two hunder an forty day an i be three day makin up my indent when she go to dry dock. all tell mark you it be this side o three hunder pound to be preceese two hunder an eighty six pound four shilling. there s not another man could ha nurse the breslau for eight month to that tune. never again never again. they may send their boat to the bottom for aught i care. 
there s no need say janet softly. we re do wi holdock steiner & chase. 
it s irritatin janet it s just irritatin. i ha be justify from first to last a the world know but but i canna forgie em. ay wisdom be justify o her child. an any other man than me wad ha make the indent eight hunder. hay be our skipper ye ll have meet him. they shift him to the torgau an bid me wait for the breslau under young bannister. ye ll obsairve there d be a new election on the board. i hear the share be sellin hither an yon an the major part of the board be new to me. the old board would ne er ha do it. they trust me. but the new board be all for reorganisation. young steiner steiner s son the jew be at the bottom of it an they do not think it worth their while to send me word. the first i know an i be chief engineer be the notice of the line s winter sailin s and the breslau time for sixteen day between port an port. sixteen day man. she s a good boat but eighteen be her summer time mark you. sixteen be sheer flytin kitin nonsense an so i tell young bannister. 
we ve get to make it he say. ye should not ha send in a three hunder pound indent. 
do they look for their boat to be run on air. i say. the board s daft. 
e en tell em so he say. i m a marry man an my fourth s on the way now she say. 
a boy wi red hair janet put in. her own hair be the splendid red gold that go with a creamy complexion. 
my word i be an angry man that day. forbye i be fond o the old breslau i look for a little consideration from the board after twenty year service. there be board meetin on wednesday an i sleep overnight in the engine room takin figure to support my case. well i put it fair and square before them all. gentleman i say i ve run the breslau eight season an i believe there s no fault to find wi my wark. but if ye haud to this i waggle the advertisement at em this that i ve never hear of it till i read it at breakfast i do assure you on my professional reputation she can never do it. that be to say she can for a while but at a risk no thinkin man would run. 
what the deil d ye suppose we pas your indent for. say old holdock. man we re spendin money like watter. 
i ll leave it in the board s hand i say if two hunder an eighty seven pound be anything beyond right and reason for eight month. i might ha save my breath for the board be new since the last election an there they sit the damn deevidend huntin ship chandler deaf a the adder o scripture. 
we must keep faith wi the public say young steiner. 
keep faith wi the breslau then i say. she s serve you well an your father before you. she ll need her bottom restiffenin an new bed plate an turnin out the forward boiler an re turnin all three cylinder an refacin all guide to begin with. it s a three month job. 
because one employee be afraid. say young steiner. maybe a piano in the chief engineer s cabin would be more to the point. 
i crush my cap in my hand an thank god we d no bairn an a bite put by. 
understand gentleman i say. if the breslau be make a sixteen day boat ye ll find another engineer. 
bannister make no objection say holdock. 
i m speakin for myself i say. bannister ha bairn. an then i lose my temper. ye can run her into hell an out again if ye pay pilotage i say but ye run without me. 
that s insolence say young steiner. 
at your pleasure i say turnin to go. 
ye can consider yourself dismiss. we must preserve discipline among our employee say old holdock an he look round to see that the board be with him. they know nothin god forgie em an they nod me out o the line after twenty year after twenty year. 
i go out an sit down by the hall porter to get my wit again. i m thinkin i swear at the board. then auld mcrimmon o mcnaughten & mcrimmon come oot o his office that s on the same floor an look at me proppin up one eyelid wi his forefinger. ye know they call him the blind deevil forbye he onythin but blind an no deevil in his dealin s wi me mcrimmon o the black bird line. 
what s here mister mcphee. say he.

they ll pay more for the breslau i say. get off my knee ye smotherin beast.

so i hear say mcrimmon. ha ye ony objection to a tramp freighter. it s only fifteen a month but they say the blind deevil feed a man good than others. she s my kite. come ben. ye can thank dandie here. i m no use to thank. an noo say he what possess ye to throw up your berth wi holdock. 
the new timin say i. the breslau will not stand it.

he pucker his dry face an twist in his chair. the warld an a say he. my god the vara warld an a. but what ha you or me to do wi virginity this late along. 
this i say. there s just one thing that each one of u in his trade or profession will not do for ony consideration whatever. if i run to time i run to time barrio always the risk o the high sea. le than that under god i have not do. more than that by god i will not do. there s no trick o the trade i m not acquaint wi. 
so i ve hear say mcrimmon dry a a biscuit.

there be some more talk an next week i go aboard the kite twenty five hunder ton simple compound a black bird tramp. the deep she ride the good she d steam. i ve snap a much a eleven out of her but eight point three be her fair normal. good food forward an good aft all indent pass wi out marginal remark the best coal new donkey and good crew. there be nothin the old man would not do except paint. that be his deeficulty. ye could no more draw paint than his last teeth from him. he d come down to dock an his boat a scandal all along the watter an he d whine an cry an say they look all he could desire. every owner ha his non plus ultra i ve obsairved. paint be mcrimmon s. but you could get round his engine without riskin your life an for all his blindness i ve see him reject five flaw intermediate one after the other on a nod from me. an his cattle fittin s be guarantee for north atlantic winter weather. ye ken what that mean. mcrimmon an the black bird line god bless him. 
oh i forget to say she would lie down an fill her forward deck green an snore away into a twenty knot gale forty five to the minute three an a half knot an hour the engine runnin sweet an true a a bairn breathin in it sleep. bell be skipper. an forbye there s no love lose between crew an owner we be fond o the auld blind deevil an his dog an i m thinkin he like u. he be worth the windy side o twa million sterlin an no friend to his own blood kin. money s an awfu thing overmuch for a lonely man. 
i d take her out twice there an back again when word come o the breslau s breakdown just a i prophesy. calder be her engineer he s not fit to run a tug down the solent and he fairly lift the engine off the bed plate an they fell down in heap by what i hear. so she fill from the after stuffin box to the after bulkhead an lay star gaze with seventy nine squealin passenger in the saloon till the camaralzaman o ramsey & gold s cartagena line give her a tow to the tune o five thousand seven hunder an forty pound wi cost in the admiralty court. she be helpless ye ll understand an in no case to meet ony weather. five thousand seven hunder an forty pound with cost an exclusive o new engine. they d ha do good to ha keep me on the old timin. 
but even so the new board be all for retrenchment. young steiner the jew be at the bottom of it. they sack men right an leave that would not eat the dirt the board give em. they cut down repair. they feed crew wi leavin s an scrapin s. and reversin mcrimmon s practice they hide their defeeciencies wi paint an cheap gildin. quem deus vult perrdere prrius dementat ye remember. 
in january we go to dry dock an in the next dock lay the grotkau their big freighter that be the dolabella o piegan piegan & walsh s line in a clyde build iron boat a flat bottom pigeon breast under engined bull nose bitch of a five thousand ton freighter that would neither steer nor steam nor stop when ye ask her. while she d attend to her helm while she d take charge while she d wait to scratch herself an while she d buttock into a dockhead. but holdock and steiner have buy her cheap and paint her all over like the hoor o babylon an we call her the hoor for short. by the way mcphee keep to that name throughout the rest of his tale. so you must read accordingly. i go to see young bannister he have to take what the board give him an he an calder be shift together from the breslau to this abortion an talkin to him i go into the dock under her. her plate be pit till the men that be paint paint paintin her laugh at it. but the warst be at the last. she d a great clumsy iron twelve foot thresher propeller aitcheson design the kite and just on the tail o the shaft behind the bos be a red weepin crack ye could ha put a penknife to. man it be an awful crack. 
when d ye ship a new tail shaft. i say to bannister. 
he know what i mean. oh yon s a superfeecial flaw say he not lookin at me.

it come on to blow when we fetch soundin s an that keep me standin by the hawser lash to the capstan breathin twixt green sea. i near die o cauld an hunger for the grotkau tow like a barge an bell howkit her along through or over. it be vara thick up channel too. we be standin in to make some sort o light an we near walk over twa three fishin boat an they cry u we be overclose to falmouth. then we be near cut down by a drunken foreign fruiter that be blunderin between u an the shore and it get thick an thick that night an i could feel by the tow bell do not know whaur he be. losh we know in the morn for the wind blow the fog oot like a candle an the sun come clear. and a surely a mcrimmon gi me my cheque the shadow o the eddystone lay across our tow rope. we be that near ay we be that near. bell fetch the kite round with the jerk that come close to tearin the bitt out o the grotkau an i mind i thank my maker in young bannister s cabin when we be inside plymouth breakwater. 
the first to come aboard be mcrimmon wi dandie. do i tell you our order be to take anything we find into plymouth. the auld deil have just come down overnight puttin two an two together from what calder have tell him when the liner land the grotkau s men. he have preceesely hit oor time. i d hail bell for something to eat an he send it o er in the same boat wi mcrimmon when the auld man come to me. he grin an slap his leg and work his eyebrow the while i eat.

he succeed to admiration. he learn not to redecorate holt hangar though he warm it. to leave his guest alone. to refrain from superfluous introduction. to abandon manner of which he have great store and to hold fast by manner which can after labour be acquire. he learn to let other people hire for the purpose attend to the duty for which they be pay. he learn this he get from a ditcher on the estate that every man with whom he come in contact have his decree position in the fabric of the realm which position he would do well to consult. last mystery of all he learn to golf well. and when an american know the innermost mean of don t press slow back and keep your eye on the ball he be for practical purpose denationalise.

a child of six be tell himself story a he lay in bed. it be a new power and he keep it a secret. a month before it have occur to him to carry on a nursery tale leave unfinished by his mother and he be delight to find the tale a it come out of his own head just a surprise a though he be listen to it all new from the begin. there be a prince in that tale and he kill dragon but only for one night. ever afterwards georgie dub himself prince pasha giant killer and all the rest. you see he could not tell any one for fear of be laugh at. and his tale fade gradually into dreamland where adventure be so many that he could not recall the half of them. they all begin in the same way or a georgie explain to the shadow of the night light there be the same start off place a pile of brushwood stack somewhere near a beach. and round this pile georgie find himself run race with little boy and girl. these end ship run high up the dry land and open into cardboard box. or gild and green iron railing that surround beautiful garden turn all soft and could be walk through and overthrow so long a he remember it be only a dream. he could never hold that knowledge more than a few second ere thing become real and instead of push down house full of grow up people. a just revenge. he sit miserably upon gigantic door step try to sing the multiplication table up to four time six. 
the princess of his tale be a person of wonderful beauty. she come from the old illustrate edition of grimm now out of print. and a she always applaud georgie s valour among the dragon and buffalo he give her the two fine name he have ever hear in his life annie and louise pronounce annieanlouise. when the dream swamp the story she would change into one of the little girl round the brushwood pile still keep her title and crown. she saw georgie drown once in a dream sea by the beach. it be the day after he have be take to bathe in a real sea by his nurse. and he say a he sink. poor annieanlouise. she ll be sorry for me now. but annieanlouise walk slowly on the beach call ha. ha. say the duck laugh which to a wake mind might not seem to bear on the situation. it console georgie at once and must have be some kind of spell for it raise the bottom of the deep and he wad out with a twelve inch flower pot on each foot. a he be strictly forbid to meddle with flower pot in real life he felt triumphantly wicked. 
* * * * *. 
the movement of the grow up whom georgie tolerate but do not pretend to understand remove his world when he be seven year old to a place call oxford on a visit. here be huge building surround by vast prairie with street of infinite length and above all something call the buttery which georgie be die to see because he know it must be greasy and therefore delightful. he perceive how correct be his judgment when his nurse lead him through a stone arch into the presence of an enormously fat man who ask him if he would like some bread and cheese. georgie be use to eat all round the clock so he take what buttery give him and would have take some brown liquid call auditale but that his nurse lead him away to an afternoon performance of a thing call pepper s ghost. this be intensely thrill. people s head come off and fly all over the stage and skeleton dance bone by bone while mr. pepper himself beyond question a man of the bad wave his arm and flap a long gown and in a deep bass voice. georgie have never hear a man sing before. tell of his sorrow unspeakable. some grow up or other try to explain that the illusion be make with mirror and that there be no need to be frighten. georgie do not know what illusion be but he do know that a mirror be the look glass with the ivory handle on his mother s dress table. therefore the grow up be just say thing after the distress custom of grow up and georgie cast about for amusement between scene. next to him sit a little girl dress all in black her hair comb off her forehead exactly like the girl in the book call alice in wonderland which have be give him on his last birthday. the little girl look at georgie and georgie look at her. there seem to be no need of any further introduction. 
i ve get a cut on my thumb say he. it be the first work of his first real knife a savage triangular hack and he esteem it a most valuable possession. 
i m tho thorry. she lisp. let me look pleathe. 
there s a di ack lum plaster on but it s all raw under georgie answer comply. 
dothent it hurt. her grey eye be full of pity and interest. 
awf ly. perhaps it will give me lockjaw. 
it lookth very horrid. i m tho thorry. she put a forefinger to his hand and hold her head sidewise for a good view. 
here the nurse turn and shake him severely. you mustn t talk to strange little girl master georgie. 
she isn t strange. she s very nice. i like her an i ve show her my new cut. 
the idea. you change place with me. 
she move him over and shut out the little girl from his view while the grow up behind renew the futile explanation. 
i be not afraid truly say the boy wriggle in despair. but why don t you go to sleep in the afternoon same a provost of oriel. 
georgie have be introduce to a grow up of that name who sleep in his presence without apology. georgie understand that he be the most important grow up in oxford. hence he strive to gild his rebuke with flattery. this grow up do not seem to like it but he collapse and georgie lay back in his seat silent and enrapture. mr. pepper be sing again and the deep ring voice the red fire and the misty wave gown all seem to be mix up with the little girl who have be so kind about his cut. when the performance be end she nod to georgie and georgie nod in return. he speak no more than be necessary till bedtime but meditate on new color and sound and light and music and thing a far a he understand them. the deep mouth agony of mr. pepper mingle with the little girl s lisp. that night he make a new tale from which he shamelessly remove the rapunzel rapunzel let down your hair princess gold crown grimm edition and all and put a new annieanlouise in her place. so it be perfectly right and natural that when he come to the brushwood pile he should find her wait for him her hair comb off her forehead more like alice in wonderland than ever and the race and adventure begin. 
ten year at an english public school do not encourage dream. georgie win his growth and chest measurement and a few other thing which do not appear in the bill under a system of cricket foot ball and paper chase from four to five day a week which provide for three lawful cut of a grind ash if any boy absent himself from these entertainment. he become a rumple collar dusty hat fag of the low third and a light half back at little side foot ball. be push and prod through the slack backwater of the low fourth where the raffle of a school generally accumulate. win his second fifteen cap at foot ball enjoy the dignity of a study with two companion in it and begin to look forward to office a a sub prefect. at last he blossom into full glory a head of the school ex officio captain of the game. head of his house where he and his lieutenant preserve discipline and decency among seventy boy from twelve to seventeen. general arbiter in the quarrel that spring up among the touchy sixth and intimate friend and ally of the head himself. when he step forth in the black jersey white knickers and black stocking of the first fifteen the new match ball under his arm and his old and fray cap at the back of his head the small fry of the low form stand apart and worship and the new cap of the team talk to him ostentatiously that the world might see. and so in summer when he come back to the pavilion after a slow but eminently safe game it matter not whether he have make nothing or a once happen a hundred and three the school shout just the same and woman folk who have come to look at the match look at cottar cottar major. that s cottar. above all he be responsible for that thing call the tone of the school and few realise with what passionate devotion a certain type of boy throw himself into this work. home be a faraway country full of pony and fish and shoot and men visitor who interfere with one s plan. but school be the real world where thing of vital importance happen and crisis arise that must be deal with promptly and quietly. not for nothing be it write let the consul look to it that the republic take no harm and georgie be glad to be back in authority when the holiday end. behind him but not too near be the wise and temperate head now suggest the wisdom of the serpent now counsel the mildness of the dive. lead him on to see more by half hint than by any direct word how boy and men be all of a piece and how he who can handle the one will assuredly in time control the other. 
for the rest the school be not encourage to dwell on it emotion but rather to keep in hard condition to avoid false quantity and to enter the army direct without the help of the expensive london crammer under whose roof young blood learn too much. cottar major go the way of hundred before him. the head give him six month final polish teach him what kind of answer best please a certain kind of examiner and hand him over to the properly constitute authority who pass him into sandhurst. here he have sense enough to see that he be in the low third once more and behave with respect toward his senior till they in turn respect him and he be promote to the rank of corporal and sit in authority over mix people with all the vice of men and boy combine. his reward be another string of athletic cup a good conduct sword and at last her majesty s commission a a subaltern in a first class line regiment. he do not know that he bore with him from school and college a character worth much fine gold but be please to find his mess so kindly. he have plenty of money of his own. his train have set the public school mask upon his face and have teach him how many be the thing no fellow can do. by virtue of the same train he keep his pore open and his mouth shut. 
the regular work of the empire shift his world to india where he taste utter loneliness in subaltern s quarter one room and one bullock trunk and with his mess learn the new life from the begin. but there be horse in the land pony at reasonable price. there be polo for such a could afford it. there be the disreputable remnant of a pack of hound. and cottar worry his way along without too much despair. it dawn on him that a regiment in india be near the chance of active service than he have conceive and that a man might a well study his profession. a major of the new school back this idea with enthusiasm and he and cottar accumulate a library of military work and read and argue and dispute far into the night. but the adjutant say the old thing. get to know your men young un and they ll follow you anywhere. that s all you want know your men. cottar think he know them fairly well at cricket and the regimental sport but he never realise the true inwardness of them till he be send off with a detachment of twenty to sit down in a mud fort near a rush river which be span by a bridge of boat. when the flood come they go forth and hunt stray pontoon along the bank. otherwise there be nothing to do and the men get drink gamble and quarrel. they be a sickly crew for a junior subaltern be by custom saddle with the bad men. cottar endure their riot a long a he could and then send down country for a dozen pair of box glove. 
i wouldn t blame you for fightin say he if you only know how to use your hand. but you don t. take these thing and i ll show you. the men appreciate his effort. now instead of blaspheme and swear at a comrade and threaten to shoot him they could take him apart and soothe themselves to exhaustion. a one explain whom cottar find with a shut eye and a diamond shape mouth spit blood through an embrasure. we try it with the glove sir for twenty minute and that do u no good sir. then we take off the glove and try it that way for another twenty minute same a you show u sir an that do u a world o good. t wasn t fightin sir. there be a bet on. 
cottar dare not laugh but he invite his men to other sport such a race across country in shirt and trouser after a trail of tear paper and to single stick in the evening till the native population who have a lust for sport in every form wish to know whether the white men understand wrestle. they send in an ambassador who take the soldier by the neck and throw them about the dust. and the entire command be all for this new game. they spend money on learn new fall and hold which be good than buy other doubtful commodity. and the peasantry grin five deep round the tournament. 
that detachment who have go up in bullock cart return to headquarter at an average rate of thirty mile a day fair heel and toe. no sick no prisoner and no court martial pending. they scatter themselves among their friend sing the praise of their lieutenant and look for cause of offense. 
how do you do it young un. the adjutant ask. 
oh i sweat the beef off em and then i sweat some muscle on to em. it be rather a lark. 
if that s your way of lookin at it we can give you all the lark you want. young davy isn t feelin quite fit and he s next for detachment duty. care to go for him. 
sure he wouldn t mind. i don t want to shove myself forward you know. 
you needn t bother on davy s account. we ll give you the sweepin s of the corp and you can see what you can make of em.

that account for mr. elery sayin i be workin my nice new boy too hard say a wing commander.

not cottar. i ve only run across one of his muster before a fellow call ingles in south africa. he be just the same hard train athletic sport build of animal. always keep himself in the pink of condition. didn t do him much good though. shoot at wesselstroom the week before majuba. wonder how the young un will lick his detachment into shape. 
cottar turn up six week late on foot with his pupil. he never tell his experience but the men speak enthusiastically and fragment of it leak back to the colonel through sergeant batman and the like. 
there be great jealousy between the first and second detachment but the men unite in adore cottar and their way of show it be by spar him all the trouble that men know how to make for an unloved officer. he seek popularity a little a he have seek it at school and therefore it come to him. he favour no one not even when the company sloven pull the company cricket match out of the fire with an unexpected forty three at the last moment. there be very little get round him for he seem to know by instinct exactly when and where to head off a malingerer. but he do not forget that the difference between a daze and sulky junior of the upper school and a bewilder browbeat lump of a private fresh from the depot be very small indeed. the sergeant see these thing tell him secret generally hide from young officer. his word be quote a barrack authority on bet in canteen and at tea. and the veriest shrew of the corp burst with charge against other woman who have use the cook range out of turn forbear to speak when cottar a the regulation ordain ask of a morning if there be any complaint.

no thank. i ve get a fight on with the major. the virtuous apprentice sit up till midnight in the major s quarter with a stop watch and a pair of compass shift little paint lead block about a four inch map. 
then he turn in and sleep the sleep of innocence which be full of healthy dream. one peculiarity of his dream he notice at the begin of his second hot weather. two or three time a month they duplicate or run in series. he would find himself slide into dreamland by the same road a road that run along a beach near a pile of brushwood. to the right lay the sea sometimes at full tide sometimes withdraw to the very horizon. but he know it for the same sea. by that road he would travel over a swell of rise grind cover with short wither grass into valley of wonder and unreason. beyond the ridge which be crown with some sort of street lamp anything be possible. but up to the lamp it seem to him that he know the road a well a he know the parade grind. he learn to look forward to the place. for once there he be sure of a good night s rest and indian hot weather can be rather try. first shadowy under close eyelid would come the outline of the brushwood pile. next the white sand of the beach road almost overhang the black changeful sea. then the turn inland and uphill to the single light. when he be unrestful for any reason he would tell himself how he be sure to get there sure to get there if he shut his eye and surrender to the drift of thing. but one night after a foolishly hard hour s polo. the thermometer be  in his quarter at ten o clock. sleep stand away from him altogether though he do his best to find the well know road the point where true sleep begin. at last he saw the brushwood pile and hurry along to the ridge for behind him he felt be the wide awake sultry world. he reach the lamp in safety tingle with drowsiness when a policeman a common country policeman spring up before him and touch him on the shoulder ere he could dive into the dim valley below. he be fill with that just beyond him in the valley lay the light of the city of sleep where he would have be shelter and that this policeman thing have full power and authority to head him back to miserable wakefulness. he find himself look at the moonlight on the wall drip with fright. and he never overcome that horror though he meet the policeman several time that hot weather and his come be the but other dream perfectly absurd one fill him with an incommunicable delight. all those that he remember begin by the brushwood pile. for instance he find a small clockwork steamer. he have notice it many night before. lie by the sea road and step into it whereupon it move with surpass swiftness over an absolutely level sea. this be glorious for he felt he be explore great matter. and it stop by a brushwood pile say his companion. and all his trouble be at an end. he take a pony because he understand that this be the thirty mile ride and he must ride swiftly and race through the clatter tunnel and round the curve always downhill till he hear the sea to his leave and saw it rag under a full moon against sandy cliff. it be heavy go but he recognise the nature of the country the dark purple down inland and the bent that whistle in the wind. the road be eat away in place and the sea lash at him black foamless tongue of smooth and glossy roller. but he be sure that there be le danger from the sea than from them whoever they be inland to his right. he know too that he would be safe if he could reach the down with the lamp on it. this come a he expect. he saw the one light a mile ahead along the beach dismount turn to the right walk quietly over to the brushwood pile find the little steamer have return to the beach whence he have unmoored it and must have fall asleep for he could remember no more. i m gettin the hang of the geography of that place he say to himself a he shave next morning. i must have make some sort of circle. let s see. the thirty mile ride. now how the deuce do i know it be call the thirty mile ride. join the sea road beyond the first down where the lamp be. and that atlas country lie at the back of the thirty mile ride somewhere out to the right beyond the hill and tunnel. rummy thing dream. wonder what make mine fit into each other so. 
he continue on his solid way through the recur duty of the season. the regiment be shift to another station and he enjoy road march for two month with a good deal of mix shoot throw in and when they reach their new cantonment he become a member of the local tent club and chase the mighty boar on horseback with a short stab spear. there he meet the mahseer of the poonch beside whom the tarpon be a a herring and he who land him can say that he be a fisherman. this be a new and a fascinate a the big game shoot that fell to his portion when he have himself photograph for the mother s benefit sit on the flank of his first tiger. 
then the adjutant be promote and cottar rejoice with him for he admire the adjutant greatly and marvel who might be big enough to fill his place. so that he nearly collapse when the mantle fell on his own shoulder and the colonel say a few sweet thing that make him blush. an adjutant s position doe not differ materially from that of head of the school and cottar stand in the same relation to the colonel a he have to his old head in england. only temper wear out in hot weather and thing be say and do that try him sorely and he make glorious blunder from which the regimental sergeant major pull him with a loyal soul and a shut mouth. sloven and incompetent rag against him. the weak mind strive to lure him from the way of justice. the small mind yea men whom cottar believe would never do thing no fellow can do impute motif mean and circuitous to action that he have not spend a think upon. and he taste injustice and it make him very sick. but his consolation come on parade when he look down the full company and reflect how few be in hospital or cell and wonder when the time would come to try the machine of his love and labour. 
but they need and expect the whole of a man s work day and maybe three or four hour of the night. curiously enough he never dream about the regiment a he be popularly suppose to. the mind set free from the day s do generally cease work altogether or if it move at all carry him along the old beach road to the down the lamp post and once in a while to terrible policeman day. the second time that he return to the world s lose continent. this be a dream that repeat itself again and again with variation on the same grind. he know that if he only sit still the person from the lily lock would help him and he be not disappoint. sometimes he be trap in mine of vast depth hollow out of the heart of the world where men in torment chant echo song. and he hear this person come along through the gallery and everything be make safe and delightful. they meet again in low roof indian railway carriage that halt in a garden surround by gild and green railing where a mob of stony white people all unfriendly sit at breakfast table cover with rose and separate georgie from his companion while underground voice sing deep voice song. georgie be fill with enormous despair till they two meet again. they foregather in the middle of an endless hot tropic night and creep into a huge house that stand he know somewhere north of the railway station where the people eat among the rose. it be surround with garden all moist and drip. and in one room reach through league of whitewash passage a sick thing lay in bed. now the least noise georgie know would unchain some wait horror and his companion know it too. but when their eye meet across the bed georgie be disgust to see that she be a child a little girl in strap shoe with her black hair comb back from her forehead. 
what disgraceful folly. he think. now she could do nothing whatever if it head come off. 
then the thing cough and the ceiling shatter down in plaster on the mosquito net and they rush in from all quarter. he drag the child through the stifle garden voice chant behind them and they ride the thirty mile ride under whip and spur along the sandy beach by the boom sea till they come to the down the lamp post and the brushwood pile which be safety. very often dream would break up about them in this fashion and they would be separate to endure awful adventure alone. but the most amuse time be when he and she have a clear understand that it be all make believe and walk through mile wide roar river without even take off their shoe or set light to populous city to see how they would burn and be rude a any child to the vague shadow meet in their ramble. late in the night they be sure to suffer for this either at the hand of the railway people eat among the rose or in the tropic upland at the far end of the thirty mile ride. together this do no much affright them. but often georgie would hear her shrill cry of boy. boy. half a world away and hurry to her rescue before they maltreat her. 
he and she explore the dark purple down a far inland from the brushwood pile a they dare but that be always a dangerous matter. the interior be fill with them and they go about sing in the hollow and georgie and she felt safe on or near the seaboard. so thoroughly have he come to know the place of his dream that even wake he accept it a a real country and make a rough sketch of it. he keep his own counsel of course. but the permanence of the land puzzle him. his ordinary dream be a formless and a fleet a any healthy dream could be but once at the brushwood pile he move within know limit and could see where he be go. there be month at a time when nothing notable cross his sleep. then the dream would come in a batch of five or six and next morning the map that he keep in his write case would be write up to date for georgie be a most methodical person. there be indeed a danger his senior say so of his develop into a regular auntie fuss of an adjutant and when an officer once take to old maidism there be more hope for the virgin of seventy than for him. 
but fate send the change that be need in the shape of a little winter campaign on the border which after the manner of little campaign flash out into a very ugly war. and cottar s regiment be choose among the first. 
now say a major this ll shake the cobweb out of u all especially you galahad. and we can see what your hen with one chick attitude ha do for the regiment. 
cottar nearly weep with joy a the campaign go forward. they be fit physically fit beyond the other troop. they be good child in camp wet or dry feed or unfed. and they follow their officer with the quick suppleness and train obedience of a first class foot ball fifteen. they be cut off from their apology for a base and cheerfully cut their way back to it again. they crown and clean out hill full of the enemy with the precision of well break dog of chase. and in the hour of retreat when hamper with the sick and wound of the column they be persecute down eleven mile of waterless valley they serve a rearguard cover themselves with a great glory in the eye of fellow professional. any regiment can advance but few know how to retreat with a sting in the tail. then they turn to make road most often under fire and dismantle some inconvenient mud redoubt. they be the last corp to be withdraw when the rubbish of the campaign be all sweep up. and after a month in stand camp which try moral severely they depart to their own place in column of four sing. 
e s goin to do without em don t want em any more. e s goin to do without em a e s often do before. e s goin to be a martyr on a ighly novel plan an all the boy and girl will say ow. what a nice young man man man. ow. what a nice young man. 
there come out a gazette in which cottar find that he have be behave with courage and coolness and discretion in all his capacity. that he have assist the wound under fire and blow in a gate also under fire. net result his captaincy and a brevet majority couple with the distinguish service order. 
a to his wound he explain that they be both heavy men whom he could lift more easily than any one else. otherwise of course i should have send out one of my men. and of course about that gate business we be safe the minute we be well under the wall. but this do not prevent his men from cheer him furiously whenever they saw him or the mess from give him a dinner on the eve of his departure to england. a year s leave be among the thing he have snaffle out of the campaign i to use his own word. the doctor who have take quite a much a be good for him quote poetry about a good blade carve the casque of men and so on and everybody tell cottar that he be an excellent person. but when he rise to make his maiden speech they shout so that he be understand to say it isn t any use tryin to speak with you chap rottin me like this. let s have some pool.

it be not unpleasant to spend eight and twenty day in an easy go steamer on warm water in the company of a woman who let you see that you be head and shoulder superior to the rest of the world even though that woman may be and most often be ten count year your senior. p. o. boat be not light with the disgustful particularity of atlantic liner. there be more phosphorescence at the bow and great silence and darkness by the hand steer gear aft. 
awful thing might have happen to georgie but for the little fact that he have never study the first principle of the game he be expect to play. so when mr. zuleika at aden tell him how motherly an interest she felt in his welfare medal brevet and all georgie take her at the foot of the letter and promptly talk of his own mother three hundred mile near each day of his home and so forth all the way up the red sea. it be much easy than he have suppose to converse with a woman for an hour at a time. then mr. zuleika turn from parental affection speak of love in the abstract a a thing not unworthy of study and in discreet twilight after dinner demand confidence. georgie would have be delight to supply them but he have none and do not know it be his duty to manufacture them. mr. zuleika express surprise and unbelief and ask those question which deep ask of deep. she learn all that be necessary to conviction and be very much a woman resume. georgie never know that she have abandon. the motherly attitude. 
do you know she say somewhere in the mediterranean i think you re the very dear boy i have ever meet in my life and i d like you to remember me a little. you will when you be old but i want you to remember me now. you ll make some girl very happy. 
oh. hope so say georgie gravely. but there s heap of time for marryin an all that sort of thing ain t there.
